Witness Retraction and Liability: The Principle of Non-Compensation for Marital Rights
Ruling on witness retraction in divorce after consummation

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi usul principle that rights without property equivalent are not compensable when witnesses retract testimony in divorce cases.

Core Idea
Marital rights (milku al-bid'ah) are not property; their loss due to false testimony is uncompensable.

This passage from Nur al-Anwar examines a specific scenario: witnesses testify to a divorce after consummation, the qadi rules separation and mahr, then witnesses retract. The Hanafi ruling is that the husband cannot claim compensation from the witnesses for the loss of marital rights. Why? Because the right of sexual access (milku al-bid'ah) is not considered property and has no equivalent. This illustrates a key usul principle: only rights that have a monetary equivalent can be the basis for liability when lost due to false testimony.

Guided Path
1
Identify the case
Two witnesses testify that a husband gave three divorces after consummation. The qadi rules separation and payment of mahr. Then the witnesses retract, saying no divorce occurred.
2
Identify the loss to the husband
The husband loses two things: (1) the mahr he paid (but it was already due due to consummation), and (2) his right to marital relations (milku al-bid'ah).
The mahr was already obligatory; thus it is not a loss caused by the testimony.
3
Apply the principle of non-compensation for non-property rights
The loss of milku al-bid'ah is not compensable because it has no equivalent in wealth. It is not property like food or money except in the context of marriage, and even then only for new consideration (mahr), not for compensation.
Hanafi usul: only losses that have a known equivalent (mithl) are subject to daman (guarantee).
4
Contrast with the pre-consummation case
If the divorce testimony was before consummation, the witnesses would be liable for half the mahr because before consummation there was a possibility the mahr could be dropped; the testimony confirmed the half mahr, causing a definite loss.
Key difference: here the loss is of a definite monetary right (half mahr), which has an equivalent.
5
Extract the underlying usul rule
The principle: 'Ma la mithla lahu la yudman' — what has no equivalent cannot be made liable. This is derived from the nature of marital rights as non-property.
This rule governs many areas of Hanafi fiqh, especially in testimonies and liabilities.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : وملک النكاح لا يضمى بالشهادة بالطلاق بعد
الدخول
ای اصول پر تیسری تفریع یہ اٹھاتے ہیں کہ اگر دوا دومیوں نے گواہی دی کہ فلاں نے دخول کے بعد بیوی کو تین طلاقیں دیدیں ہیں اور قاضی نے مہر کے ادا کرنے اور افتراق کا فیصلہ
کر دیا ہے پھر گواہوں نے اپنی گواہی سے رجوع کر لیا کہ اس نے طلاقیں نہیں دی تھیں ۔ تو ہمارے نزدیک شوہر ان گواہوں سے کسی قسم کا مطالبہ نہیں کرے گا اس لئے کہ مہر تو شوہر پر جماع (ولی) کی وجہ سے واجب ہو چکا تھا خواہ وہ طلاق دیتا ہو یا نہ دیتا ہو ان گواہوں کی وجہ سے شوہر کو صرف یہ نقصان ہوا کہ ملک بضعہ فوت ہو گئی ہے لیکن بضعہ کا کوئی مثل نہیں کیونکہ اگر طعہ کا مثل بضعہ کو بناتے ہیں تو یہ حرام ہے اور اگر بضعہ کا مشل مال کو بناتے ہے تو یہ جائز نہیں اس لئے کہ بضعہ کے بدلے میں مال ضرورت کی بنا پر صرف نکاح میں دیا جاتا ہے۔ نکاح کے علاوہ کہیں بھی مال کار ینا سیج نہیں ۔ جماع کی قید ہم نے اس لئے لگائی کہ اگر گواہوں نے گواہی دی کہ اس نے جماع سے پہلے طلاق دی تو اس صورت میں گواہ نصف مہر کے ضامن ہونگے اسلئے کہ جماع سے پہلے احتمال تھا۔ کہ شاید کسی
عذر کی وجہ سے مہر ساقط ہو جائے مگر طلاق کی گواہی کی وجہ سے نصف مہر مؤکد ہو گیا اس لئے اس نصف مہر کا مطالبہ ان گواہوں سے کیا جائے گا۔
His saying: 'And the right of marriage (milku al-nikah) is not guaranteed by testimony of divorce after consummation.' On this principle, a third branch is derived: if two men testify that so-and-so gave three divorces to his wife after consummation, and the qadi rules payment of mahr and separation, then the witnesses retract their testimony saying he did not divorce. Then in our view, the husband will not claim anything from these witnesses, because the mahr was already due on the husband due to intercourse (wati'), whether he divorced or not. The only loss to the husband is that the right of marital authority (milku al-bid'ah) is lost, but bid'ah has no equivalent. If we make food the equivalent of bid'ah, it is haram; if we make wealth its equivalent, it is not permissible because wealth is given in exchange for bid'ah only in marriage out of necessity, not elsewhere. We have conditioned intercourse because if the witnesses testified that he divorced before intercourse, then in that case they are liable for half the mahr, because before intercourse there was possibility that the mahr might be dropped due to some excuse, but due to the divorce testimony, half the mahr became confirmed, so that half can be claimed from the witnesses.
Source pages p. 95

Commentary
This passage continues applying the principle that what has no equivalent carries no guarantee. The case: witnesses testify to triple divorce after consummation; the qadi issues a ruling; the witnesses retract. The husband loses only the right to marital relations (milku al-bid'ah), which has no equivalent in property. Thus, the witnesses are not liable for that loss. However, if the divorce was before consummation, the witnesses would be liable for half the mahr because before consummation there was a possibility that the mahr might fall due to an annulment; the testimony confirmed half the mahr, thus the witnesses caused that loss.

Key Terms
ملک البضع (milku al-bid'ah): The husband's right to sexual access in marriage.
مهر (mahr): Bridal gift due from husband to wife.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In Hanafi law, if witnesses testify to divorce after consummation and later retract, why are they not liable for the loss of marital rights?
A) Because the husband was already divorced.
B) Because marital rights have no equivalent in wealth.
C) Because the qadi's ruling is final.
D) Because the witnesses acted in good faith.

Key Takeaway
Loss of marital rights due to false testimony is not compensable in Hanafi law because those rights have no property equivalent.

Does Performance Prove Permissibility? The Hanafi vs Mutakallimun Debate
Debate whether performing a commanded act establishes permissibility

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position that performing a commanded act establishes permissibility, and evaluate the mutakallimun's qiyas-based objection.

Core Idea
Mere performance of a commanded act establishes its permissibility unless proven otherwise.

This passage examines a foundational usul dispute: does the act of performing a commanded duty automatically confer the attribute of jawaz (permissibility)? The Hanafi position relies on the default assumption of validity (istishab), while some mutakallimun argue that external verification is needed. The debate has practical implications for how we judge acts performed by others.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi/Jumhur position
Identify the majority view: mere performance establishes permissibility and negation of dislike. This is the 'sahih' according to the fuqaha.
The text says 'al-sahih 'inda al-fuqaha'.
2
Identify the mutakallimun's objection
Some mutakallimun hold that permissibility is not established without external evidence confirming all conditions were fulfilled.
They require a dalil khariji (external evidence).
3
Analyze the mutakallimun's qiyas
They analogize to a corrupt hajj: a pilgrim who has intercourse before Arafah must still complete the rites, but his hajj is not permissible (valid). Thus, performance alone does not guarantee permissibility.
The qiyas uses the corrupt hajj case as the original (asl).
4
Evaluate the Hanafi response
The Hanafis distinguish: in the corrupt hajj, there is external evidence (intercourse) that invalidates the act. Without such evidence, performance stands as prima facie evidence of validity.
This invokes istishab al-hal (presumption of continuity of original permissibility).
5
Derive the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical difference: a person praying behind an imam without verifying his conditions. Hanafis judge the prayer valid; mutakallimun would suspend judgment until conditions are verified.
This affects daily practice of following imams.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : وهل تثبت صفة الجواز للمامور به اذا أتى به قال بعض المتكلمين لا والصحيح عند الفقهاء إنه تثبت به صفة الجواز للما موربه وانتفاء الكراهة. ماموریہ کے لئے صفت جواز کب ثابت ہوگی : جب مکلف شخص مامور به کوادا کرے تو محض ادا کرنے سے بعض علماء کہتے ہیں کہ مامور بہ کیلئے جواز کی صفت ثابت ہو جائیگی یعنی ہم یہ فیصلہ کریں گے کہ مامور بہ ادا ہو گیا اور یہی جمہور کا مذ ہب ہے۔ لیکن بعض متکلمین یہ کہتے ہیں کہ جب تک کوئی ایسی خارجی دلیل نہ پائی جائے جو اس بات پر دلالت کرتے کہ مکلف نے ساری شرائط کا لحاظ رکھا ہے، اس وقت تک ہم اس مامور بہ پر جواز کا حکم نہیں لگائیں گے۔ دلیل متکلمین وہ قیاس کرتے ہیں کہ اگر کوئی شخص وقوف عرفہ سے پہلے جماع کے ذریعے حج فاسد کر دے تو اسے حکم دیا جائے گا کہ وہ باقی ارکان کو بھی دیگر حجاج کی طرح ادا کرے لیکن اس کے باوجود اس کے لئے جواز کی صفت باقی نہیں ہوتی لیکن ملا ، کہتے ہیں کہ صرف افعال کے کرنے سے اس کے لئے جواز کی صفت ثابت ہو
He said: 'And is the attribute of permissibility established for the commanded act when one performs it?' Some mutakallimun say no, and the correct view according to the jurists is that the attribute of permissibility for the commanded act and the negation of dislike are established by it. When the obligated person performs the commanded act, some scholars say that merely by performing it, the attribute of permissibility is established for the commanded act, meaning we will judge that the commanded act has been performed, and this is the way of the majority. But some mutakallimun say that until an external evidence is found that indicates that the obligated person observed all conditions, we will not apply the ruling of permissibility to that commanded act. The evidence of the mutakallimun is that they analogize: if a person makes his hajj corrupt by intercourse before the standing at Arafah, he will be commanded to perform the remaining rituals like other pilgrims, yet despite that, the attribute of permissibility does not remain for him. But the [scholars] say that merely by performing the acts, the attribute of permissibility is established for him.
Source pages p. 102

Commentary
This passage addresses a usul dispute: when a person performs a commanded act, is the attribute of permissibility (jawaz) automatically established for that act? The majority of jurists (jumhur al-fuqaha) hold that yes, mere performance indicates the act is permissible and valid. However, some mutakallimun (theologians) argue that without external evidence that all conditions were fulfilled, we cannot rule permissibility. They analogize from a case where a pilgrim commits a prohibited act (intercourse) before Arafah, rendering his hajj corrupt (fasid). Even though he is ordered to continue and complete the remaining rites, his act does not attain the attribute of permissibility — his hajj remains invalid. The text then mentions that 'mala' (possibly 'the scholars' or 'the jurists') counter that performing the acts alone establishes permissibility. The passage appears to favor the majority view, noting it is the 'sahih' (correct) position among jurists. This dispute reflects deeper usul differences about default assumptions (istishab) and the burden of proof.

Key Terms
صفة الجواز (sifat al-jawaz): The attribute of permissibility, indicating the act is legally valid and not disliked

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the majority of jurists mentioned, when does the attribute of permissibility (jawaz) become established for a commanded act?
A) Only when external evidence confirms all conditions are met.
B) Merely by performing the act.
C) Only after a judge issues a ruling.
D) Only if the act is performed in congregation.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi usul, performing a commanded act is itself sufficient to establish its permissibility unless there is concrete evidence of invalidity.

Disagreement on the Measure of Deficient Time (Juz' Naqis)
Recording Hanafi internal disagreement on deficient time measure

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between the majority Hanafi view and Imam Zufar's view on the deficient time (juz' naqis) and explain the talil based on taklif ma la yutaq.

Core Idea
The Hanafi definition of deficient time avoids impossible obligations (taklif ma la yutaq), not completing the prayer.

This lesson examines an internal Hanafi ikhtilaf regarding the measure of juz' naqis, the deficient time at the end of a prayer window. The majority restricts it to the time for the opening takbir, while Imam Zufar expands it to four rak'ahs. Understanding this dispute reveals how the usul principle of taklif ma la yutaq constrains definitions and shapes practical rulings.

Guided Path
1
Pinpoint the legal question
What is the measure of deficient time (juz' naqis) at the end of the prayer window? Both sides agree it is the time remaining such that the prayer becomes obligatory in that time if started then.
2
Memorize the majority Hanafi answer
The majority (Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, Muhammad) define deficient part as the amount sufficient for the opening takbir (approx 1-2 minutes).
This minimizes the time and avoids imposing a full prayer obligation in a very short window.
3
Know Imam Zufar's alternative answer
Imam Zufar defines deficient part as the amount sufficient for four rak'ahs of 'Asr (approx 4-6 minutes).
This ensures that the prayer can be performed fully if started at the last moment.
4
Trace the shared talil
Both sides justify their definition by the principle of avoiding taklif ma la yutaq (imposing an impossible obligation). The majority argues a larger juz' naqis would make full performance impossible; Zufar argues a smaller juz' naqis would make complete performance impossible.
The disagreement is about what is considered 'possible' or 'impossible' in the remaining time.
5
Apply the dispute to a scenario
Consider 'Asr prayer near sunset. If the prayer becomes nullified after starting in the deficient time, does it need to be repeated? According to the majority: no, because no time remains (deficient time is too short for a repeat). According to Zufar: yes, because the deficient time is large enough to allow a repeat of four rak'ahs.
This thamarah al-khilaf shows the practical impact of the definition.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
جزء ناقص کی مقدار میں اختلاف ائمہ :
احناف کے نزدیک اتنی مقدار جس میں نماز کا احرام باندھا جا سکے جس کا اندازہ تقریباً ایک یا دو منٹ ہے امام زفرحنفی کے نزدیک اتنی مقدار جس میں عصر کی چار رکعتیں اداء کی جا سکیں جسکا اندازہ چارتے چھ منٹ ہے بہر دوصورت اب سمیت منتقل نہ ہوگی کیونکہ ایسی صورت میں ایک ایسی چیز کا مکلف بنانا لازم آئے گا جس کی ادائیگی ناممکن ہو تو تکلیف مالا طاق ہے۔ پھر نماز اگر وقت کامل میں واجب ہو اور درمیان میں فساد پیش آجائے تو نماز باطل ہو جا ئے گی۔ جیسے فجر میں ہوتا ہے اور اگر نا قص وقت میں واجب ہو تو فساد پیش آجانے سے نماز باطل نہ ہوگی جیسے کہ نماز عصر میں ہوتا ہے۔
Disagreement of imams on the measure of deficient part: According to the Hanafis, it is that measure in which the opening takbir of prayer can be performed, estimated at approximately one or two minutes. According to Imam Zufar al-Hanafi, it is that measure in which four rak'ahs of 'Asr can be performed, estimated at four to six minutes. In both cases, the obligation does not transfer (?) because in such a case it would be necessary to make someone responsible for a thing whose performance is impossible, and that is declaring responsibility for the impossible (taklif ma la yutaq). Then, if the prayer becomes obligatory in complete time and corruption occurs in the middle, the prayer becomes invalid, as in Fajr. And if it becomes obligatory in deficient time, then upon occurrence of corruption the prayer does not become invalid, as in 'Asr prayer.
Source pages p. 107

Commentary
This passage presents an internal Hanafi dispute on the definition of 'deficient time' (juz' naqis). The consensus of the Hanafi school (Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, Muhammad) defines the deficient part as that sufficient only for the opening takbir, roughly one to two minutes. Imam Zufar, however, defines it as sufficient for four rak'ahs of 'Asr, about four to six minutes. The reasoning for both views is to avoid taklif ma la yutaq (imposing impossible obligations): making the deficient part too large would make the prayer impossible if time runs out. The passage then highlights a consequence: If a prayer becomes obligatory in complete time (like Fajr) and then becomes corrupt (e.g., nullified), the prayer is invalid because there was full time to redo it. But if it became obligatory in deficient time (like 'Asr at the end of its time) and becomes corrupt, the prayer is not invalid because there is no time left to repeat; the obligation was already on the deficient part. This shows the practical impact of the definition.

Key Terms
جزء ناقص (juz' naqis): The deficient portion of time at the end of the prayer window.
تکلیف مالا یطاق (taklif ma la yutaq): Imposing an obligation that cannot be performed, which is invalid in Islamic law.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the majority of Hanafi scholars (Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, Muhammad), what is the minimum amount of time defined as 'deficient part' for 'Asr?
A) Enough for one rak'ah
B) Enough for the opening takbir (approx 1-2 min)
C) Enough for four rak'ahs (approx 4-6 min)
D) Enough for three rak'ahs

Key Takeaway
The internal Hanafi dispute over juz' naqis demonstrates how the usul principle of avoiding taklif ma la yutaq shapes divergent definitions, with the majority view being the operative position.

The Traveler's Intention: Hanafi Dispute on the Nature of Concession
Ruling on the traveler and sick person intending a wajib or nafl fast other than Ramadan.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the Hanafi position and the Sahibayn's objection regarding the traveler's intention for a wajib fast other than Ramadan, and apply the usul principle of 'time as a standard (mi'yar)' to distinguish between real excuse and ruling concession.

Core Idea
The traveler's concession is a ruling concession, not a real excuse, so he retains the choice to fast another wajib.

This passage examines an intra-Hanafi dispute on whether a traveler may intend a wajib fast other than Ramadan. The disagreement hinges on the nature of the concession: is it a delegation of choice or a waiver of obligation upon use? The Sahibayn argue that the concession is for ease; if the traveler chooses to fast, the original obligation returns. Imam Abu Hanifa holds that the concession drops the obligation entirely, allowing the traveler to substitute another fast. This dispute reveals deeper usul principles about how concessions operate and the distinction between real and ruling excuses.

Guided Path
1
Identify the parties
Who are the disputants? Imam Abu Hanifa (the matn) and the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani).
The Sahibayn are often in agreement against Abu Hanifa on this issue.
2
State the point of conflict
Can a traveler intend a wajib fast other than Ramadan (e.g., qada or kaffara) while in Ramadan?
3
Analyze the Hanafi proof
Abu Hanifa argues that the traveler's Ramadan fast is saqit (dropped) due to the rukhsat (concession). Since the obligation is removed, he has the choice to fast another wajib or not fast at all.
The concession is taken as a hukm (ruling) that completely lifts the obligation.
4
Analyze the Sahibayn's proof
The Sahibayn argue that the rukhsat is for ease; if the traveler does not avail it, the original obligation returns. Therefore, if he fasts, it must be the Ramadan fast.
They treat the concession as a conditional permission, not a removal.
5
Apply the dichotomy to the sick person
Unlike the traveler, the sick person's concession is based on a real excuse (udhr haqiqi). If he fasts another wajib despite illness, it shows he is not incapacitated, so the original ruling applies and his fast is Ramadan.
This distinction is key: traveler's concession is hukmi, sick person's is haqiqi.
6
Note the two narrations on nafl
There are two narrations from Abu Hanifa on whether a traveler may intend a nafl fast. One allows it (Hasan ibn Ziyad), the other disallows (Ibn Sama'a) based on priority of wajib over nafl.
This shows the issue is not settled within the school.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله الا فى المسافر ينوى واجباً آخر عند أبي حنيفة رحمه الله تعالى بخلاف المريض وفى النقل عنه روايتان. امام ابو حنیفہ کے نزدیک مسافر واجب آخر کی نیت کر سکتا ہے۔ مثالا قضاء کفارہ وغیرہ کی کیونکہ مسافر سے رمضان المبارک کا روزہ ساقط ہے، تو لہذا اس کو اختیار ہے کہ چاہے کھائے نے یا چاہے تو کوئی دوسرا واجب روزہ رکھے مثلا قضاء رمضان یا کفارہ کا روزہ لیکن صاحبین کے نزدیک مسافر کیلئے دوسرا روزہ رکھنا بھی جائز نہیں ہے اس لئے کہ اس کو رخصت دی گئی تھی آسانی کیلئے لیکن اس نے جب رخصت پر عمل نہیں کیا تو حکم اپنے اصل کی طرف لوٹ آئیگا اور رمضان ہی کا روزہ اس پر فرض ہو گا جیسے دوسرے لوگوں پر فرض ہے۔ لیکن اگر بیمار شخص فرض روزے کے علاوہ کسی دوسرے روزے کی نیت کرلے تو تعلق عمر حقیقی کے ساتھ ہو گا بخلاف مسافر کے کہ وہاں مدار رخصت بجز حکمی ہے لہذا تو سب وہ بیماری کے باوجود کوئی دوسرا روزہ رکھ رہا ہے تو معلوم ہوا کہ وہ عاجز نہیں ہے۔ لہذا حکم اصلی لوٹ آئے گا اور اس کا روزہ رمضان ہی کا ہوگا۔ جہاں تک روزہ رکھنے کی صورت میں مریض کی بیماری کے بڑھ جانے کے خوف کا تعلق ہے تو بعض لوگوں نے ان دونوں باتوں میں یوں تطبیق دی ہے کہ اگر ایسی بیماری ہو جس کو روزہ نقصان دیتا ہے تو اسکا تعلق بحجز تقدیری کے ساتھ ہے اور اگر ایسی بیماری ہو جس کو روزہ نقصان نہیں دیتا ہو تو اس کا تعلق بحجر حقیقی کے ساتھ ہے۔ اگر مسافر بجائے کسی واجب آخر کے نفل کی نیت سے روزہ رکھے تو اس شخص کے بارے میں امام صاحب سے دو روایتیں ہیں امام حسن بن زیادہ کی روایت کے مطابق مسافر نفلی روزہ رکھ سکتا ہے کیونکہ اللہ تعالیٰ نے اس کو افطار کی رخصت دی ہے جبکہ دوسری روایت کے مطابق جو ابن سماعہ کی ہے وہ نفلی روزہ نہیں رکھ سکتا بلکہ روزہ رمضان ہی کا ہو گا اس لئے کہ اس کو افطار کی رخصت دی گئی تھی استراحت اور آرام کیلئے لیکن اگر وہ استراحت نہیں چاہتا تو دین کے منافع حاصل کرے اور وہ یہ ہے کہ جو اس پر قضاء یا کفارہ واجب ہے وہ روزہ رکھے کیونکہ اگر وہ اس رمضان میں فوت ہو جائے تو اس سے رمضان کے روزوں کے بارے میں سوال نہیں ہو گا لیکن قضا اور کفارہ کے روزوں کے بارے میں سوال ہو گا لیکن نفلی روزہ کی یہ اہمیت نہیں لہذا مسافر نفلی روزہ نہیں رکھ سکتا۔ قوله أو يكون معياراً لا سبباً لقضاء رمضان والنذر المطلق
His statement: 'Except that a traveler may intend another wajib according to Abu Hanifa, may Allah have mercy on him, unlike the sick person, and there are two narrations from him.' Imam Abu Hanifa says a traveler can intend another wajib, e.g., qada or kaffara, because the Ramadan fast is dropped from him; so he has the option to eat or to keep another wajib fast like qada or kaffara. But the Sahibayn say that keeping another fast is not permissible for the traveler because he was given a concession for ease; when he does not act on the concession, the ruling returns to its original, and the Ramadan fast becomes obligatory on him just as on others. However, if a sick person intends a fast other than the obligatory one, it relates to a real excuse, unlike the traveler where the basis is a ruling concession. So if despite illness he keeps another fast, it shows he is not incapacitated; therefore the original ruling returns and his fast will be of Ramadan. As for the fear of increased illness when fasting, some have reconciled both matters as follows: if it is an illness that fasting harms, then it relates to a presumptive hindrance; if fasting does not harm it, then it relates to a real hindrance. If a traveler intends a voluntary (nafl) fast instead of another wajib, there are two narrations from Imam Abu Hanifa. According to the narration of Hasan ibn Ziyad, the traveler can keep a voluntary fast because Allah gave him the concession to break the fast. According to the other narration of Ibn Sama'a, he cannot keep a voluntary fast; rather the fast will be Ramadan, because the concession was given for rest and ease, but if he does not want rest, he should gain the benefits of religion, i.e., keep what is obligatory upon him like qada or kaffara, because if he dies in this Ramadan, he will not be questioned about Ramadan fasts but will be questioned about qada and kaffara. A voluntary fast does not have this importance, so the traveler cannot keep a voluntary fast. His statement: 'Or that it is a standard, not a cause, for qada of Ramadan and absolute vows.'
Source pages p. 109

Commentary
This passage deals with a specific fiqh issue arising from the usul principle that time is a standard. The matn quotes the ruling that a traveler may intend a wajib fast other than Ramadan according to Imam Abu Hanifa, but not the sick person. The commentary explains the reasoning: for the traveler, the Ramadan fast is not obligatory (saqit) due to the concession, so he is free to either not fast or to fast another wajib. The Sahibayn argue that the concession is for ease; if he chooses to fast, the original obligation (Ramadan) returns. For the sick person, his concession is based on actual inability, so if he fasts another wajib, it shows he is able, and thus the Ramadan fast applies. The text also mentions two narrations regarding voluntary fasts: Hasan ibn Ziyad allows it, Ibn Sama'a disallows it on grounds of priority. The final matn statement distinguishes between time being a standard (mi'yar) vs. a cause (sabab) for qada and absolute vows.

Key Terms
رخصت (rukhsat): A concession granted by Shariah allowing a traveler not to fast in Ramadan.
عذر حقیقی (udhr haqiqi): A genuine excuse based on actual incapacity, such as illness that makes fasting harmful.
معیار (mi'yar): A standard or measure; in this context, time serves as a standard for determining when an obligation is due, as opposed to being a cause (sabab) for the obligation itself.
سبب (sabab): A cause that brings about a legal obligation. In the context of vows, the time may be a cause for fulfilling the vow.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the source text, what is the key difference between the traveler's and the sick person's concessions?
A) The traveler's concession is based on a real excuse, the sick person's is a ruling concession.
B) The traveler's concession is a ruling concession, the sick person's is based on a real excuse.
C) Both are based on real excuses.
D) Both are ruling concessions.

Key Takeaway
The key distinction is between a real excuse (udhr haqiqi) and a ruling concession (rukhsat hukmi); the former reinstates the original obligation when the excuse ends, while the latter entirely removes the obligation.

The Fourth Type of Time-Bound Command: the Mushkil Time of Hajj
Usul dispute over the fourth type of time-bound command

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the characteristics of a mushkil (ambiguous) time-bound command and apply the Hanafi usul analysis to determine the obligation of Hajj in light of the Abu Yusuf-Muhammad ikhtilaf.

Core Idea
When time is both container and criterion, it is mushkil; the Hanafi school has a valid internal ikhtilaf on its consequence.

In the Hanafi usul tradition, time-bound commands are classified based on how time relates to the commanded act. The fourth type is the most subtle: a time that is both wider than necessary (like a container) and yet restrictive (allowing only one performance, like a criterion). Hajj provides the classic example, leading to a disagreement between Abu Yusuf and Muhammad on when the obligation must be fulfilled. This lesson unpacks that ambiguity and its practical implications.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its time category
Recognize that Hajj is a once-in-a-lifetime obligation with a designated season. Note that the time span (Shawwal, Dhu al-Qa'dah, first ten days of Dhu al-Hijjah) is wider than the actual performance period.
The time is 'mushkil' because it resembles both a container and a criterion.
2
Deconstruct the twofold ambiguity
First ambiguity: the time is longer than needed (container) but only one Hajj fits (criterion). Second ambiguity: life expectancy makes time either wide (many years) or narrow (if death comes soon).
3
Analyze Abu Yusuf's position
He emphasizes the potential narrowness: since death may occur before the next season, Hajj becomes obligatory immediately in the first year. Delaying without excuse leads to fisq and rejection of testimony.
His reasoning is based on caution (ihtiyat) and the principle that obligations with uncertain time must be performed promptly.
4
Analyze Muhammad's position
He emphasizes the general width: a person may live many years, so the obligation is absolute (mutlaq) and can be delayed as long as it is eventually performed without being missed.
He analogizes to other absolute obligations like zakat, which can be delayed.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf and mufta bihi
The practical difference: Abu Yusuf's view renders a delayer fasiq and his testimony rejected; Muhammad's view does not. The mufta bihi may follow Abu Yusuf due to caution.
Both positions are valid within the Hanafi school.

Source Text

قوله : أو يكون مشكلاً يشبه المعيار والظرف ويتأدى باطلاق النية لا بنية النفل ويتعين اشهر الحج من العام الاول عند ابو يوسف خلافا لمحمد

امر موقت کی قسم رابع :

امر موقت کی چوتھی قسم یہ ہے کہ مامور بہ کا وقت مشکل اور مشتبہ الحال ہو مشکل ہونے کا معنی یہ ہے کہ اس میں اشتباہ ہو کہ ایک اعتبار سے وہ ظرف کے مشابہ ہو اور دوسرے اعتبار سے وہ معیار سے مشابہ ہو جیسا کہ حج کا وقت یہ دو طریقوں سے مشکل اور مشتبہ الحال ہے کیونکہ جب ہم اس بات کو دیکھتے ہیں کہ حج کا وقت ڈھائی مہینے "شوال، ذیقعدہ ، اور ذی الحجہ کے دکھ روز " ہیں لیکن حج صرف ذی الحجہ کے چند دنوں یعنی پہلے عشرے میں ادا ہوتا ہے لہذا ماقبل کے مہینے ضرورت سے زائد ہوئے تو ہم کہتے ہیں کہ وقت ظرف ہے اور جب ہم اس بات کو دیکھتے ہیں کہ اس تمام عرصے میں صرف ایک ہی حج ادا ہو سکتا ہے تو ہم کہتے ہیں کہ وقت معیار ہے دوسرا اشتباہ یہ ہے کہ ساری زندگی میں صرف ایک حج فرض ہے اگر کوئی شخص حج فرض ہونے کے بعد بنی سال زندہ ہے تو اس کے لئے وقت وسیع ہے جب چاہے حج کر سکتا ہے لیکن اگر وہ حج فرض ہو جانے کے اگلے سال زندہ نہ رہے تو اس کے لئے وقت تنگ ہے یعنی اگر ورثاء کو وصیت بھی نہیں کی تھی اور مر گیا تو گناہ گار ہوگا۔

امام ابو یوسف اس تنگی کا اعتبار کرتے ہوئے کہتے ہیں کہ پہلے سال ہی حج ادا کرنا ضروری ہے کیونکہ اگلے سال زندہ رہنا یقینی نہیں ہے جب کہ امام محمد وسعت کا اعتبار کرتے ہوئے کہتے ہیں کہ جب چاہے ادا کر سکتا ہے مگر شرط یہ ہے کہ اس کا حج فوت نہ ہو۔

ثمره اختلاف

اس اختلاف کا نتیجہ یہ نکلے گا کہ امام ابو یوسف کے نزدیک تاخیر کرنے والا مخفص فاسق اور مردود الشهادة ہوگا لیکن اگر اس نے حج کیا تو دوبارہ اس کی گواہی قبیر
His statement: 'Or it is ambiguous, resembling both a criterion and a container, and it is fulfilled by absolute intention and not by voluntary intention, and the months of Hajj are determined from the first year according to Abu Yusuf, contrary to Muhammad.' Fourth type of time-bound command: The fourth type of time-bound command is that the time of the commanded act is ambiguous and unclear. The meaning of being ambiguous is that there is ambiguity: in one respect it resembles a container, and in another respect it resembles a criterion, like the time of Hajj. It is ambiguous in two ways: first, when we look at the fact that the time of Hajj is two and a half months (Shawwal, Dhu al-Qa'dah, and the first ten days of Dhu al-Hijjah), but Hajj is only performed in a few days of Dhu al-Hijjah, i.e., the first ten days. So the preceding months are surplus to need; thus we say the time is a container. And when we look at the fact that in this entire period only one Hajj can be performed, we say the time is a criterion. Second ambiguity: there is only one obligatory Hajj in a lifetime. If a person lives many years after Hajj becomes obligatory, for him the time is wide; he can perform it whenever he wishes. But if he does not survive the year after Hajj becomes obligatory, the time is narrow for him, meaning if he did not even bequeath it and died, he would be sinful. Imam Abu Yusuf, considering this narrowness, says that performing Hajj in the first year is necessary because survival to the next year is not certain. Imam Muhammad, considering the width, says he may perform it whenever he wishes, provided that his Hajj is not missed. Result of the difference: The consequence of this difference is that, according to Abu Yusuf, the one who delays is considered a fasiq (transgressor) and his testimony is rejected, but if he then performs Hajj, his testimony is accepted (again).
Source pages p. 112

Commentary
This passage discusses the fourth type of time-bound command (amr muwaqqat), characterized by its problematic or ambiguous (mushkil) time. The time of Hajj is presented as the example. The ambiguity is twofold: (1) The appointed time spans two and a half months (Shawwal, Dhu al-Qa'dah, and the first ten days of Dhu al-Hijjah), but the actual pilgrimage (wuquf and most rites) occurs only in the first ten days of Dhu al-Hijjah. Thus the time appears to be a container (zarf)—more than needed. Yet during this entire period only one Hajj can be performed, making it also a criterion (miyar)—only one act fits. (2) Hajj is obligatory once in a lifetime. If one lives many years after the obligation, the time is wide (wasi'). But if death occurs the next year, time is narrow (dayyiq). This leads to a disagreement between the two leading students of Abu Hanifa. Abu Yusuf emphasizes the potential narrowness: since one may die before performing it, it becomes obligatory immediately in the first year. Delaying without excuse renders one a fasiq and the testimony is rejected. Muhammad al-Shaybani considers the general width (the many years one might live) and allows delay as long as one eventually performs it without letting it be lost entirely. The practical consequence (thamarah al-khilaf) is the ruling on the delayed individual's character and legal testimony. The text ends mid-sentence but implies that after performing Hajj, his testimony becomes acceptable again.

Key Terms
مشکل (mushkil): Ambiguous; having more than one possible interpretation; in this context, the time of Hajj is difficult to classify as purely container or criterion.
ظرف (zarf): Container; a time period that is wider than necessary for the act, acting only as a vessel.
معیار (miyar): Criterion; a time period that exactly measures the act, not allowing more than one performance.
ثمره اختلاف (thamarah al-khilaf): The practical consequence of a scholarly disagreement; in this case, the effect on the person's character and legal testimony.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the source, which scholar considers the potential narrowness of time due to uncertainty of life?
A) Imam Abu Hanifa
B) Imam Abu Yusuf
C) Imam Muhammad
D) Imam al-Shafi'i

Key Takeaway
The time of Hajj is mushkil (ambiguous), and the Hanafi school contains a legitimate ikhtilaf on whether it must be performed immediately or can be delayed.

Ikhtilaf — Scholarly Disagreement
advanced
10 min
The Fourth Type of Timed Command (Mushkil): Ruling and Intra-Hanafi Dispute
Explaining the fourth type of timed command (mushkil) and its ruling with disputes

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the fourth type of timed command (mushkil) and explain how the dual nature of the time (measure/container) determines the ruling on intention, and state the ikhtilaf between Abu Yusuf and Muhammad regarding the deadline for Hajj.

Core Idea
When the time is both measure and container, absolute intention suffices for obligation but supererogatory intention does not.

This passage introduces the fourth category of timed commands in Hanafi usul al-fiqh: the ambiguous or problematic (mushkil) command. Using the example of Hajj, the author illustrates how a single commanded act can have a time that is both a container (zarf) and a measure (miyar), leading to nuanced rules about intention and deadlines. The passage also presents the intra-Hanafi dispute between Abu Yusuf and Muhammad on whether Hajj must be performed immediately, and contrasts the Hanafi position with that of Imam al-Shafi'i on the effect of intending supererogatory worship.

Guided Path
1
Define the fourth type
Identify that the fourth type is the 'mushkil' timed command: its time is ambiguous, resembling both a container (broad period) and a measure (specific count). Understand the two forms of ambiguity in Hajj's time.
The passage mentions two ambiguities: time spanning months vs. single occurrence, and lifetime obligation vs. uncertainty of life.
2
Distinguish container vs. measure
Analyze how the time of Hajj functions as a container (the entire season is the period) and as a measure (only one Hajj is possible in that period). Relate to similar acts: fasting (measure) and prayer (container).
As a measure, absolute intention suffices; as a container, specific obligation intention is needed.
3
Apply the dual nature to intention
Derive the ruling: for this type, absolute intention (e.g., intending Hajj without specifying fard or nafl) fulfills the obligation, but intending supererogatory does not. Compare to fasting (measure) and prayer (container).
This is the Hanafi position, opposed by Shafi'i.
4
Examine the deadline dispute
Understand the ikhtilaf between Abu Yusuf (immediate performance in first year due to uncertainty of life) and Muhammad (permissible delay as long as one does not miss Hajj entirely).
The practical consequence (thamarah) is on fasiq status and shahada acceptance.
5
Recognize the cross-madhhab ikhtilaf
Note that Imam al-Shafi'i holds that intending supererogatory still counts as fulfilling the obligation, unlike the Hanafis. Understand the Hanafi response based on the measure vs. container analogy.
This highlights how usul principles lead to different fiqh rulings.

قوله : أو يكون مشكلاً يشبه المعيار والظرف ويتأدى باطلاق النية لا بنية النفل ويتعين اشهر الحج من العام الاول عند ابو يوسف خلافا لمحمد

امر موقت کی قسم رابع :

امر موقت کی چوتھی قسم یہ ہے کہ مامور بہ کا وقت مشکل اور مشتبہ الحال ہو مشکل ہونے کا معنی یہ ہیکہ اس میں اشتباہ ہو کہ ایک اعتبار سے وہ ظرف کے مشابہ ہو اور دوسرے اعتبار سے دو معیار سے مشابہ ہو جیسا کہ حج کا وقت یہ دو طریقوں سے مشکل اور مشتبہ الحال ہے کیونکہ جب ہم اس بات کو دیکھتے ہیں کہ حج کا وقت ڈھائی مہینے "شوال، ذیقعدہ ، اور ذی الحجہ کے دس روز " ہیں لیکن حج صرف ذی الحجہ کے چند دنوں یعنی پہلے عشرے میں ادا ہوتا ہے لہذا ماقبل کے مہینے ضرورت سے زائد ہوئے تو ہم کہتے ہیں کہ وقت ظرف ہے اور جب ہم اس بات کو دیکھتے ہیں ۔ کہ اس تمام عرصے میں صرف ایک ہی حج ادا ہو سکتا ہے تو ہم کہتے ہیں کہ وقت معیار ہے دوسرا اشتباہ یہ ہے کہ ساری زندگی میں صرف ایک حج فرض ہے اگر کوئی شخص حج فرض ہونے کے بعد پہلے سال زندہ ہے تو اس کے لئے وقت وسیع ہے۔ جب چاہے حج کر سکتا ہے لیکن اگر وہ حج فرض ہو جانے کے اگلے سال زندہ نہ رہے تو اس کے لئے وقت تنگ ہے۔ یعنی اگر ورثاء کو وصیت بھی نہیں کی تھی اور مر گیا تو گناہ گار ہوگا ۔

امام ابو یوسف اس تنگی کا اعتبار کرتے ہوئے کہتے ہیں کہ پہلے سال ہی حج ادا کرنا ضروری ہے کیونکہ اگلے سال زندہ رہنا یقینی نہیں ہے جب کہ امام محمد وسعت کا اعتبار کرتے ہوئے کہتے ہیں کہ جب چاہے بجا کر سکتا ہے مگر شرط یہ ہے کہ اس کا حج فوت نہ ہو ۔

ثمره اختلاف

اس اختلاف کا نتیجہ یہ نکلے گا کہ امام ابو یوسف کے نزدیک تاخیر کرنے والا مخلف فاسق اور مردود الشهادة ہوگا لیکن اگر اس نے حج کیا تو دوبارہ اس کی گواہی قبول ہوگی۔ عکس امام محمد کے نزدیک اس کا گناہ صرف موت کے وقت ہوگا ۔ تاخیر کی صورت میں کوئی فسق نہیں ہوگا۔

قسم رابع کا حکم :

امر مؤقت کی چوتھی قسم کا حکم یہ ہیکہ مطلق نیت سے ادا ہو جائے گی لیکن نفل کی نیت سے ادا نہیں ہوگی بلکہ اگر نفل کی نیت کی تو نفل ہی ادا ہو گا لیکن امام شافعی کے نزدیک اس صورت میں بھی حج فرض ہی ادا ہو گا ۔ ہم کہتے ہیں کہ چونکہ یہ قسم ظرف اور معیار دونوں کے مشابہ ہے تو معیار ہونے کی وجہ سے مطلق نیت سے ادا ہو جائے گا اس صورت میں حج مشابہ ہے روزے کے ساتھ اور ظرف ہونے کی وجہ سے نفل کی نیت سے ادا نہیں ہو گا جیسے کہ نماز فرض نفل کی نیت سے ادا نہیں ہوتی۔
He said: Or it is ambiguous, resembling the measure and the container, and it is performed by absolute intention, not by intention of supererogatory, and the months of Hajj are determined from the first year according to Abu Yusuf, contrary to Muhammad. The fourth type of timed command: The fourth type of timed command is that the time of the commanded act is problematic and ambiguous. The meaning of problematic is that there is ambiguity in it: from one perspective it resembles the container, and from another perspective it resembles two measures? Actually 'two measures' may be a mistake; likely 'the measure'. As for Hajj time, it is problematic and ambiguous in two ways: because when we look at the fact that the time of Hajj is two and a half months – Shawwal, Dhul Qa'dah, and the first ten days of Dhul Hijjah – but Hajj is only performed in a few days of Dhul Hijjah, i.e., the first ten days, so the preceding months are extra; then we say the time is a container. And when we look at the fact that in this entire period only one Hajj can be performed, then we say the time is a measure. The second ambiguity is that in one's entire life only one Hajj is obligatory. If a person is alive for many years after Hajj becomes obligatory, then for him the time is wide; he can perform Hajj whenever he wants. But if he does not remain alive in the year following the obligation of Hajj, then for him the time is narrow. That is, if he did not even make a will to the heirs and died, he would be sinful. Imam Abu Yusuf, considering this narrowness, says that it is necessary to perform Hajj in the first year itself because living the next year is not certain. While Imam Muhammad, considering the wideness, says that he can perform it whenever he wants, but the condition is that he should not miss his Hajj. Outcome of the dispute: The result of this disagreement will be that according to Imam Abu Yusuf, the one who delays is a sinful (fasiq) and his testimony is rejected, but if he performs Hajj, his testimony is accepted again. Contrary to Imam Muhammad, according to him his sin will only occur at the time of death; there is no sin (fisq) in delaying. Ruling of the fourth type: The ruling of the fourth type of timed command is that it will be performed by absolute intention, but it will not be performed by intention of supererogatory. Rather, if one intends supererogatory, then the supererogatory will be performed. But according to Imam Shafi'i, in this case too, the obligatory Hajj will be performed. We say that since this type resembles both the container and the measure, due to being a measure it will be performed by absolute intention – in this case Hajj resembles fasting – and due to being a container it will not be performed by intention of supererogatory, just as obligatory prayer is not performed by intention of supererogatory.
Source pages p. 112

Commentary
This passage discusses the fourth type of timed command (al-amr al-muwaqqat al-mushkil). The author uses the example of Hajj to illustrate how a single command can have a time that is both a measure (miyar) and a container (zarf), leading to a dispute within the Hanafi school. Imam Abu Yusuf prioritizes the narrowness of time due to uncertainty of life, thus requiring immediate performance in the first year, while Imam Muhammad prioritizes the wideness, allowing delay. The practical consequence is on the person's fasiq status and acceptance of testimony. The passage also contrasts the Hanafi position with Imam Shafi'i on the effect of intention: for this type, the Hanafis hold that intending supererogatory does not fulfill the obligation, unlike Shafi'i who argues it does. The reasoning is based on the dual nature of the time: as a measure, absolute intention suffices; as a container, specific obligation intention is required. This follows the analogy of fasting (measure) and prayer (container) respectively.

Key Terms
الأمر الموقت (al-amr al-muwaqqat): A command that is temporally specified, with a time that may be problematic.
مشكل (mushkil): Ambiguous; here the time is ambiguous between being a measure and a container.
ظرف (zarf): Container; the time period that contains the act, like the full season.
معيار (miyar): Measure; the time is limited to a specific instance, e.g., only one Hajj in the season.
ثمرة الاختلاف (thamarah al-ikhilaf): The practical consequence of a scholarly disagreement.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi ruling in the passage, if a person intends to perform Hajj with the intention of supererogatory worship, what is the outcome?
A) The Hajj counts as the obligatory Hajj because the intention is valid.
B) The Hajj counts as nafl, and the obligation remains unfulfilled.
C) The Hajj is invalid because intention must be specific.
D) The Hajj counts as obligatory only if performed in the first year.

Key Takeaway
The fourth type of timed command (mushkil) requires absolute intention for obligation; supererogatory intention does not suffice, and the deadline for Hajj is disputed between Abu Yusuf (immediate) and Muhammad (permissive delay).

Ikhtilaf — Scholarly Disagreement

Are Disbelievers Obligated to Perform Worship? A Hanafi Usul Analysis
usul dispute with critical refinement and talil

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to analyze the dispute over whether disbelievers are obligated to perform worship (wujub al-ada) and explain the Hanafi position using the argument about suqut al-ibadat.

Core Idea
Disbelievers are not commanded to perform worship that can fall away due to excuses.

A central question in usul al-fiqh is whether the commands of the Shari'ah address disbelievers regarding the performance of acts of worship in this world. Some scholars attribute to Imam al-Shafi'i and the Mashayikh of Iraq that kuffar are obligated to perform these acts. This lesson unpacks the dispute, evaluates the evidence, and clarifies why the Hanafi school takes the view it does.

Guided Path
1
Identify the core issue
The issue is whether kuffar are addressed with the obligation to perform acts of worship (wujub al-ada) in this world, or whether they are only addressed with the obligation to believe, and the commands to worship are contingent upon that belief.
2
State the opposing position and its apparent basis
The opposing view attributes to Imam al-Shafi'i and the Mashayikh of Iraq that kuffar are obligated to perform worship. The apparent basis is the general command in the Quran, such as 'Pray' (صلوا), which includes all responsible beings regardless of belief.
3
Analyze the Hanafi response
The commentator rejects this attribution by pointing to a logical inconsistency: if performance were obligatory, then the worship of a disbeliever would be valid and qada' would be required after conversion. But according to Imam al-Shafi'i, neither is true. Therefore, the command to pray must be interpreted as contingent upon the prior command to believe (آمنوا).
4
Recognize the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical consequence of the Hanafi view is that no qada' is required for missed worship after conversion. The opposing view would require qada'.
5
Locate the correct view according to the text
The passage clearly states: 'And the correct view is that they are not addressed with the performance of that which can fall away from acts of worship.' This is the relied-upon Hanafi position.

Source Text

قوله : وأمافى وجوب الاداء فى احكام الدنيا فكذلك عند البعض

His statement: 'As for the obligation of performance in the rulings of this world, it is likewise according to some.' But the commentator says: This statement does not appear correct, because according to Imam Shafi'i, neither is the worship of disbelievers valid, nor is qada' obligatory upon them after embracing Islam. Commentary
This passage addresses a dispute about whether disbelievers are commanded to perform the acts of worship in this world. Some attributed to Imam Shafi'i and the scholars of Iraq that kuffar are obligated to perform these acts (wujub al-ada). The commentator refutes this by arguing that if that were the case, then a disbeliever who converts should be required to make up missed prayers, but according to Imam Shafi'i, qada is not required. So the claim is inconsistent. The commentator suggests that the claim actually presupposes that the command to believe ('aminu') is implicit before the command to pray. The correct Hanafi view is that disbelievers are not addressed with the performance of acts of worship that can potentially fall away due to valid excuses. They divide worship into two categories: those that can be dropped due to excuses (like prayer and fasting for women in menses/postpartum) and those that cannot. The text cuts off before listing the second type.

Key Terms
وجوب الاداء (wujub al-ada): Obligation to perform an act of worship in its proper time.
سقوط العبادات (suqut al-ibadat): Falling away of obligation due to a valid excuse, such as menstruation.
آمنوا (aminu): The command to believe, which is implicitly prior to commands to worship.

Effect of Prohibition on Sensory and Shar'i Acts
Explaining division of acts and impact of nahi with Hanafi-Shafi'i dispute

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between sensory and shar'i acts, explain the Hanafi position on the effect of nahi on each, and evaluate the Shafi'i counterargument.

Core Idea
For Hanafis, prohibition on sensory acts invalidates; on shar'i acts it does not — the evil is intrinsic or circumstantial.

This passage introduces a fundamental distinction in Hanafi usul: acts are either sensory (hissiyya) or shar'i (shar'iyya). The effect of a prohibition (nahy) depends on this classification. Hanafis hold that prohibition on a sensory act renders it intrinsically evil and invalid, whereas prohibition on a shar'i act generally indicates an external evil, leaving the act valid but sinful. Imam al-Shafi'i disagreed, arguing that all prohibitions imply intrinsic evil. Understanding this dispute is key to correctly applying prohibitions in fiqh.

Guided Path
1
Define the two categories of acts
Identify the definition of sensory acts (hissiyya) and shar'i acts (shar'iyya) as given in the text. Sensory acts have fixed meanings; shar'i acts have meanings changed by Shari'a.
Sensory: killing, adultery, wine. Shar'i: prayer, fasting, sale.
2
State the Hanafi rule for each category
According to the author, nahy on sensory acts falls on the essence (qabih li-'aynihi). Nahy on shar'i acts falls on an external attribute (qabih li-ghayrihi wasfan), unless a specific proof indicates intrinsic evil.
The proof switches the category to essence, as with selling mudamin, mulamaqih, or prayer without wudu.
3
Identify the Shafi'i rule and contrast
Imam al-Shafi'i holds that prohibition on both categories implies intrinsic evil (qabih li-'aynihi). The dispute hinges on the nature of the demand (iqtida') in nahy.
Shafi'i argument: the demand of prohibition cannot be realized in a way that nullifies it.
4
Understand the Hanafi proof (linguistic reasoning)
Hanafis argue that nahy requires the servant to have choice. If the act were intrinsically evil, prohibition would negate choice, turning it into negation (nafy). For shar'i acts, since they can be performed without the prohibited attribute, the prohibition must be on that attribute.
Example: telling a blind person 'do not see' is meaningless.
5
Apply the dispute to a concrete example
Apply the thamarah al-khilaf: selling during Friday adhan. Hanafis rule the sale valid but sinful; Shafi'is rule it invalid. Trace the reasoning from each school's principle.
This shows the practical impact of the usul difference.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

افعال کی تقسیم
مصنف فرماتے ہیں کہ افعال دو قسم کے ہیں ۔
(۱) افعال حسین (۲) افعال شرعیہ

جب نہی افعال حسیہ سے آئی ہو تو وہ صحیح تعینہ پر محمول ہوگی اور اگر نہی افعال شرعیہ سے آئی ہو تو وہ فتح لغیرہ وصف پر محمول ہوگی لیکن اگر کوئی دلیل اس کی فتح لعینہ ہونے پر دلالت کرے تو اس کو صبح عید پر محمول کریں گے جیسے مضامین جمع مضمویہ اور ملاقیح ( جمع ملقوعہ ) کی بیع اور

قوله : وقال الشافعى رحمه الله فى البابين ينصرف الى
القسم الاول
امام شافعی کا مذہب ... لیکن امام شافعی فرماتے ہیں بھی افعال شرعیہ اور افعال حسیہ
دونوں سے فتح لعینہ پر تمول ہوگی
قوله : لأن القبح يثبت اقتضاء فلا يتحقق على
وجه يبطل به المقتضى احناف کی دلیل ہم کہتے ہیں کہ نھی کا معنی یہ ہے کہ بندے کو اختیار کے باوجود کسی فعل سے روکا جائے لیکن اگر اسے اختیار ہی نہ ہوں تو نہی نفی بن جائیگی جیسے اندھے سے کہا جائے (مت دیکھے ) ۔ برتن میں پانی نہ ہو اور کہا جائے کہ (مت پی ) وغیر ہ ذالک من الامثلہ ۔ .
His statement: 'And prohibition concerning sensory acts falls on the first type, and concerning shar'i matters it falls on that which has an inseparable attribute (wasfan).' Division of acts. The author says: Acts are of two types: (1) Sensory acts (af'al hissiyya), (2) Shar'i acts (af'al shar'iyya). Definition of sensory acts: They are acts whose meanings were known before the Shari'a and still remain on that meaning, like killing, adultery, drinking wine. Definition of shar'i acts: They are acts whose original meanings changed after the coming of the Shari'a, like fasting, prayer, and sale. When the prohibition pertains to sensory acts, it is carried upon their essence (qabih li-'aynihi), and if the prohibition pertains to shar'i acts, it is carried upon the external attribute (qabih li-ghayrihi wasfan). But if there is a proof indicating that they are qabih li-'aynihi, we carry it upon the essence as well, like selling of mudamin, mulamaqih, and the prayer of a person in hadath. His statement: 'And Imam al-Shafi'i (may Allah have mercy on him) said regarding both categories that the prohibition turns to the first type (i.e., essence).' Imam Shafi'i's madhhab: But Imam Shafi'i says that for both shar'i and sensory acts, the prohibition implies the act is evil in its essence. His statement: 'Because qabah (evil) is established as an iqtida' (demand), so it cannot be realized in a way that nullifies the iqtida'.' The Hanafi proof: We say that the meaning of nahi is to prevent the servant from an action despite having choice. But if there is no choice, then the nahi turns into negation, like telling a blind person 'do not see', or when there is no water in the pot and you say 'do not drink', etc.
Source pages p. 117

Commentary
This passage discusses the classification of acts into sensory (af'al hissiyya) and shar'i (af'al shar'iyya) and how prohibition applies differently to each according to the Hanafis. The Hanafis hold that if an act is purely sensory, the prohibition indicates that the act is intrinsically evil (qabih li-'aynihi) and therefore invalid. For shar'i acts, the prohibition generally indicates an external evil (qabih li-ghayrihi wasfan), meaning the act may be valid but sinful unless a proof raises it to intrinsic evil. Imam Shafi'i holds that in both cases, prohibition implies intrinsic evil. The Hanafi proof is based on linguistic reasoning: nahi assumes the servant has the ability to choose; if there is no choice, the command becomes meaningless. Thus, for sensory acts where the act is inherently evil, the prohibition is on the essence; for shar'i acts which are neutral in themselves, the prohibition must be on an external attribute.

Key Terms
افعال حسیہ (af'al hissiyya): Acts whose meanings are known through sensory perception and are not changed by Shari'a, e.g., killing, adultery.
افعال شرعیہ (af'al shar'iyya): Acts whose meanings and rulings are established by Shari'a and differ from their linguistic or sensory meanings, e.g., prayer, fasting, sale.
قبیح لعینہ (qabih li-'aynihi): An act that is evil in its essence, intrinsically prohibited.
قبح لغیرہ وصفا (qabih li-ghayrihi wasfan): An act evil due to an inseparable external attribute, not its essence.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Which of the following acts does the Hanafi school consider invalid due to prohibition?
A) Selling during Friday adhan
B) Praying without wudu
C) Eating while a guest is fasting
D) Conducting a sale during a battle

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school distinguishes between sensory acts (intrinsically evil and invalid when prohibited) and shar'i acts (externally evil but valid unless a proof indicates intrinsic evil).

Hanafi Rebuttal to Shafi'i/Maliki on Minimum Plural
Presents dispute with Shafi'i/Maliki and Hanafi responses

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to evaluate the Hanafi response to the hadith 'Al-ithnani fama fawqahuma jama'ah' and apply the principle that the minimum plural is three to commands in the Quran and Sunnah.

Core Idea
The minimum plural is three by linguistic consensus; the hadith on two is context-specific, not a general definition.

This passage addresses a key usul dispute: is the minimum number for a plural two or three? Imam Shafi'i and some Malikis cite a hadith stating 'two and above are a congregation' to argue for two. The Hanafi school, relying on the consensus of linguists (ijma' ahl al-lughah), holds that the minimum plural is three. The author provides two interpretations to reconcile the hadith with the linguistic consensus, showing that the hadith applies only to specific contexts like inheritance and prayer, not to general linguistic usage.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Disputed Issue
The issue is the minimum number of individuals that constitutes a plural (adna al-jam') in Arabic. This has direct implications for understanding general commands like 'akrimu al-rijal' (honor the men).
2
State the Shafi'i/Maliki Position and Dalil
Imam Shafi'i and some Maliki scholars claim the minimum plural is two. Their evidence is the prophetic hadith: 'Al-ithnani fama fawqahuma jama'ah' (Two and above are a congregation).
They take the hadith as a general linguistic definition.
3
State the Hanafi Position and Its Dalil
The Hanafi school holds the minimum plural is three, based on the consensus of Arabic linguists (ijma' ahl al-lughah). The singular is one, the dual is two, and plural starts from three.
This is a stronger foundation because it relies on established linguistic principles.
4
Analyze the Hanafi Response to the Opposing Hadith
The author gives two interpretations to reconcile the hadith with the linguistic consensus: (1) The hadith refers specifically to inheritance rules (e.g., two daughters receive two-thirds, just as more than two do) and wills. (2) It refers to the imam's position in prayer: if followers are three or more, the imam stands ahead; if two, they stand behind. Thus, the hadith is context-specific, not a general definition.
These interpretations preserve the consensus of linguists while honoring the hadith.
5
Apply the Principle to a Fiqh Command
Consider the general command 'akrimu al-rijal' (honor the men). According to the Hanafi view, this obligates honoring at least three men. According to Shafi'i/Maliki, honoring two would suffice. The practical thamarah al-khilaf is the minimum obligation in such commands.

Imam Shafi'i and some companions of Imam Malik (may Allah have mercy on them) say that the minimum of plural is two. Their evidence is the saying of the Prophet (peace be upon him): 'Al-ithnani fama fawqahuma jama'ah.' The author (may Allah have mercy on him) gives two answers, please observe: His statement: 'And his saying (peace be upon him) 'Al-ithnani fama fawqahuma jama'ah' is interpreted to refer to inheritance and wills or to the sunnah of the imam going ahead.' Commentary
This passage presents a dispute with Imam Shafi'i and some Maliki scholars who claim that the minimum of plural is two. Their evidence is the hadith 'Al-ithnani fama fawqahuma jama'ah' (Two and above are a congregation). The author (musannif) provides two responses. First, the hadith is interpreted to apply specifically to inheritance and wills, because in inheritance, the ruling for two shares is the same as for more than two, e.g., two daughters receive two-thirds, and two sisters similarly. Two brothers from the mother's side also shift the share from one-sixth to one-third, same as more than two. Second, the hadith is interpreted regarding the imam's position in prayer: if there are three or more followers, the imam stands ahead, but if only two, they stand behind him. This reconciles the hadith with the consensus of linguists that the minimum plural is three. The passage is cut off at the second answer, but the first answer is complete.

Key Terms
جماعة (jama‘ah): A group of people; in the context of this hadith, it is interpreted as referring to a congregation for inheritance shares or prayer position.
اقل الجمع (adna al-jam‘): The minimum number that constitutes a plural in Arabic.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Hanafi Position on 'Umum al-Mushtarak: Rejecting Simultaneous Meanings
Presents the Hanafi rejection of 'umum mushtarak and notes the Shafi'i permissibility.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on 'umum mushtarak, explain the Hanafi proof against it, and identify the practical consequence (thamarah) of this dispute in interpreting Quranic texts.

Core Idea
A mushtarak word cannot indicate all its meanings at once; only one meaning can be intended at a time.

This lesson examines a fundamental usul dispute: can a homonym (mushtarak) carry all its meanings simultaneously? The Hanafi school firmly rejects this, arguing from linguistic convention, while the Shafi'i school permits it. Understanding this disagreement is crucial for interpreting many Quranic and hadith texts where a word has multiple meanings.

Guided Path
1
Identify the disputed concept
What is 'umum mushtarak? State the Hanafi and Shafi'i positions clearly.
The text states the Hanafi position and mentions the Shafi'i view.
2
Analyze the Hanafi proof
Why do Hanafis reject simultaneous meanings? Focus on the alternative nature (ala sabil al-badal) of mushtarak.
Using a mushtarak for all meanings at once contradicts its established linguistic usage.
3
Understand the Shafi'i position
What is the Shafi'i rationale? Typically, they argue that the Lawgiver can intend all meanings if context allows.
The text cuts off, but the disagreement is clear.
4
Apply the dispute to a real example
How does this affect the interpretation of 'quru' in the Quran? Hanafis pick one meaning via qarina; Shafi'is could accept both.
The thamarah al-khilaf: different fiqh rulings on 'idda.
5
Evaluate the tarjih
Which position does the text adopt and why is it the mufta bihi in Hanafi usul?
The text clearly adopts the Hanafi view.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : ولا عموم له
(۴) عموم مشترک جائز ہے یا نہیں؟
ہمارے نزدیک مشترک میں عموم نہیں ہوتا لہذا ایک لفظ سے ایک ہی وقت میں اسکے دو یا دو سے زائد معانی مراد لینا جائز نہیں ہے۔
امام شافعی رحمہ اللہ کا مذاب امام شافعی کے نزدیک عموم مشترک جائز ہے یعنی ایک ہی وقت
His statement: 'And there is no 'umum (generality) for it.' (4) Is 'umum mushtarak permissible or not? According to us, mushtarak does not have 'umum, so it is not permissible to intend two or more of its meanings at the same time from a single word. The madhhab of Imam Shafi'i: According to Imam Shafi'i, 'umum mushtarak is permissible, meaning at the same time...
Source pages p. 142

Commentary
This passage discusses a key usul dispute between the Hanafi and Shafi'i schools regarding whether a mushtarak (homonym) can have 'umum (generality) allowing all its meanings to be intended simultaneously. The Hanafi position, expressed as 'there is no 'umum for it', holds that a mushtarak word can only indicate one of its meanings at a time, and any attempt to take multiple meanings simultaneously is invalid. This is based on the linguistic nature of mushtarak: since the word was coined for different meanings separately, using it for all at once contradicts its conventional usage. The Shafi'i position, attributed to Imam al-Shafi'i, permits 'umum mushtarak, meaning that a speaker can intend multiple meanings of a homonym at once. The dispute has practical implications for interpreting ambiguous texts in the Quran and Sunnah. For example, if the word 'quru' appears in a verse and both meanings (menstruation and purity) are claimed to be intended, Hanafis would reject that and require choice, while Shafi'is would allow both to be considered. The text does not elaborate the Shafi'i proof here, but the disagreement is clearly presented.

Key Terms
عموم مشترک (umum mushtarak): The concept that a mushtarak word can indicate all its meanings simultaneously in a general sense.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

C) It is obligatory to intend all meanings
D) It is recommended to intend the most common meaning

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school holds that a mushtarak word cannot be used for multiple meanings simultaneously, based on its alternative linguistic nature.

Reconciling Conflicting Hadith: The Grave Robber Case
Usul dispute on grave robber's hand amputation

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to evaluate the Hanafi position on hand amputation for a grave robber by reconciling conflicting hadith through the concept of siyasah (ruler's discretion).

Core Idea
Conflicting hadith are reconciled by interpreting one as siyasah rather than fixed law.

This lesson examines a classic usul dispute: should a grave robber (nabbash) have his hand amputated? The Hanafi school, led by Abu Hanifa, says no, while Abu Yusuf and Shafi'i argue for amputation based on a hadith. The resolution hinges on how to reconcile conflicting textual evidence—a core skill in usul al-fiqh.

Guided Path
1
Identify the conflicting narrations
Note the two hadith: (1) 'Whoever digs up a grave, we will cut his hand' (Man nabasha qata'na) and (2) 'No amputation for the shroud thief' (La qat'a 'ala al-mukhtafi). The first supports amputation; the second explicitly exempts the grave robber (since the shroud thief is synonymous).
This is a clear case of ta'arud al-adillah (apparent contradiction of evidences) in usul.
2
Explain the Hanafi method of reconciliation
The Hanafis do not reject the first hadith but reclassify it. They argue it was said as a matter of siyasah (ruler's discretionary punishment), not as a fixed hadd punishment. This is based on the principle that amputation is only for theft (sariqah) from a guarded place, and grave robbery does not meet that definition.
The term siyasah is key: it allows the ruler to impose punishment for public order without violating the fixed hudud.
3
Apply the concept of siyasah to derive the ruling
Since the hadith 'La qat'a 'ala al-mukhtafi' is general and authentic, and the practice of the Prophet and Caliphs consistently did not amputate grave robbers, the first hadith must be interpreted as a political threat or a policy punishment (siyasah), not a legally binding hadd. Therefore, the grave robber receives ta'zir (discretionary punishment) instead.
This shows how context and consistent practice (amal) can override the apparent meaning of a text.
4
Determine the practical outcome
In practice: Hanafi school: no hand amputation, only tazir. The opposing view (Abu Yusuf and Shafi'i): amputation. The author of the text prefers the Hanafi position.

Source Text

نباش پر قطع ید والی سزا کا جاری نہ ہونا امام اعظم ابو حنیفہ رحمہ اللہ اور ان کے متبعین کا مذہب ہے جبکہ امام ابو یوسف اور امام شافعی فرماتے ہیں کہ نباش کا ہاتھ بھی کا نا جائیگا اس لئے کہ حضور صلی اللہ علیہ وسلم نے فرمایا من نبش قطعنا ہم کہتے ہیں کہ یہ سیاست پر محمول ہے اس لئے کہ دوسری حدیث میں ہے لا قطع على المختفی - کفن چور پر قطع ید کی سزا نہیں ہے نیز حضوراکرم صلی اللہ علیہ وسلم اور خلفائے راشدین رضوان اللہ علیہم اجمعین کا بھی یہی عمل رہا ہے۔
The non-application of the punishment of hand amputation on the grave robber is the school of Imam Abu Hanifa and his followers, while Imam Abu Yusuf and Imam Shafi'i say that the hand of the grave robber will be cut, because the Prophet (peace be upon him) said: 'Whoever digs up a grave, we will cut his hand.' We say that this is interpreted as a political punishment, because in another hadith: 'No amputation for the one who steals a shroud' - there is no hand amputation for the shroud thief. Also, the practice of the Prophet and the Rightly Guided Caliphs was the same.
Source pages p. 153

Commentary
This passage discusses a dispute regarding the application of the hadd punishment of hand amputation to a grave robber (nabbash). The Hanafi position, held by Abu Hanifa and his followers, is that the grave robber's hand is not cut. The opponents, Abu Yusuf and Shafi'i, rely on a hadith that appears to command amputation for grave robbing. The Hanafi response is that this hadith is to be interpreted as a matter of siyasah (state policy/political punishment) rather than a fixed hadd punishment, because another hadith explicitly exempts the shroud thief (mukhtafi) from amputation. Moreover, the consistent practice of the Prophet and the Caliphs supports non-amputation. This ruling is part of the Hanafi school's fiqh.

Key Terms
نباش (nabbāsh): A grave robber who digs up graves to steal shrouds.
سیاست (siyāsah): Political punishment determined by ruler's discretion, not fixed hadd.

Key Terms from Source Passage

C) The Imam has a choice to cut or not.
D) He is given the same punishment as a thief.

Key Takeaway
Conflicting hadith are reconciled by interpreting one as siyasah, preserving the integrity of both texts and the established practice.

Mutashabih: Definition and the Dispute Over Its Knowability
Defines mutashabih, its ruling, and presents the dispute with Shafi'i

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to define mutashabih according to Hanafi usul, state the Hanafi ruling, and identify the point of disagreement with Imam al-Shafi'i regarding who knows its meaning.

Core Idea
Mutashabih: meaning known only to Allah; we believe it is true without interpretation.

In this passage, the author defines the fourth category of mubayyan? Actually, this is about mutashabih. The passage defines mutashabih and presents a key ikhtilaf between the Hanafi school and Imam al-Shafi'i and the Mu'tazila. Understanding this definition helps you recognize which Quranic verses and hadith are not open to ijtihad in interpretation but require simple belief.

Guided Path
1
Define mutashabih
From the text, identify the precise definition: a word whose intended meaning's recognition is cut off.
Note the Arabic: 'انقطع رجاء معرفة المراد'.
2
State the Hanafi ruling
What must a believer do with mutashabih texts? The text says: 'believe in its truth before attainment.' It is obligatory to believe it is true without interpreting it.
This is the Hanafi position.
3
Identify the opposing view
Imam al-Shafi'i and the Mu'tazila claim that the rasikhun (firmly grounded scholars) can know the meaning of mutashabih.
Cite the passage: 'و الإمام الشافعي وعامة المعتزلة يقولون...'
4
Determine the practical difference
The thamarah al-khilaf: For Hanafis, no one may interpret mutashabih; for Shafi'is, qualified scholars may do so.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : وأما المتشابه فهو اسم لما انقطع رجاء معرفة المراد منه وحكمه اعتقاد الحقية قبل الإصابة كالمقطعات في أوائل السور مثل الم حم .
قسم رابع متشابہ کی تعریف :
متشابہ اس لفظ کا نام ہے جس کی مراد کے پہنچانے کی امید ختم ہو جائے
متشابہ کا حکم :
اور اس کا حکم یہ ہے کہ قیامت سے پہلے اس کے حق ہونے کا اعتقاد کیا جائے کیونکہ
قیامت کے بعد تو پتہ چل جائیگا کہ یہ حکم امت کے لئے ہے باقی نبی علیہ الصلوۃ والسلام کو تو علم تھا ہی۔ اور امام شافعی اور عام معتزلہ حضرات کہتے ہیں کہ علماء راسخین کو بھی متشابہ کا معنی معلوم ہوتا ہے۔
He said: 'As for the mutashabih (ambiguous), it is a name for that concerning which hope of knowing the intended meaning is cut off. Its ruling is to believe in its truth before attaining understanding, like the disconnected letters at the beginnings of surahs, such as Alif Lam Mim.'
Fourth section: Definition of mutashabih:
Mutashabih is the name of a word whose intended meaning's recognition is hopeless.
Ruling of mutashabih:
And its ruling is that before the Day of Judgment, one should believe it to be true, because after the Day of Judgment it will be known whether this was a ruling for the community; as for the Prophet, he already knew. And Imam Shafi'i and the general Mu'tazila say that the firmly grounded scholars also know the meaning of mutashabih.
Source pages p. 156

Commentary
This passage defines mutashabih (ambiguous/unclear) and contrasts the Hanafi position with that of Imam Shafi'i and the Mu'tazila. The matn says: 'As for the mutashabih, it is a name for that concerning which hope of knowing the intended meaning is cut off. Its ruling is to believe in its truth before attaining understanding, like the disconnected letters at the beginning of surahs, such as Alif Lam Mim.' The commentator adds: 'The fourth section: definition of mutashabih: mutashabih is the name for a word whose intended meaning's recognition is hopeless. Its ruling: to believe it is true before the Day of Judgment, because after the Day of Judgment it will be known whether it was a ruling for the community; the Prophet knew it already. And Imam Shafi'i and the general Mu'tazila say that the firmly grounded scholars also know the meaning of mutashabih.' The Hanafi position is that only Allah knows the intended meaning, and we must believe it is true without seeking a specific interpretation. This is a key difference between the two major usul schools.

Key Terms
متشابه (mutashabih): A word concerning which hope of knowing the intended meaning is cut off; its true meaning is known only to Allah.
راسخون في العلم (rasikhun fi al-ilm): The firmly grounded scholars; in the dispute, Shafi'i holds they know the meaning of mutashabih.

Key Terms from Source Passage

B) Only the Prophet and the Caliphs knew them.
C) Only Allah knows their true meaning.
D) The firmly grounded scholars know them.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi usul, mutashabih texts have a true meaning known only to Allah; we believe they are true and do not interpret them.

Ikhtilaf — Scholarly Disagreement
