Intention in Wudu: A Usul Dispute on Haqiqah and Majaz
Usul dispute over textual interpretation and intention in wudu

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi usul principles of haqiqah and majaz to interpret a disputed hadith and derive the ruling on intention in wudu.

Core Idea
The same hadith yields opposite rulings when one school reads literally and the other metaphorically.

This passage presents a classic usul al-fiqh dispute between the Hanafi and Shafi'i schools over whether intention (niyyah) is a mandatory element (fard) of wudu. At the heart of the disagreement lies the interpretation of the Prophet's hadith: 'رفع عن أمتي الخطأ والنسيان' ('My ummah is relieved of error and forgetfulness'). The Hanafis argue that this hadith, understood metaphorically, shows that the worldly validity of acts like wudu does not depend on intention. The Shafi'is, however, insist on a general (umum) reading that requires intention. Understanding this dispute requires grasping two usul concepts: haqiqah (literal meaning) and majaz (metaphorical meaning), and how context (qarina) can shift interpretation.

Guided Path
1
Identify the disputed ruling
State the issue clearly: Is intention (niyyah) a fard (obligatory element) of wudu? Determine the position of each school.
The Hanafi position: intention is not fard. The Shafi'i position: intention is fard.
2
Locate the Hanafi dalil
Find the primary evidence cited by the Hanafis: the hadith 'رفع عن أمتي الخطأ والنسيان'. Note that this is a hadith ahad (zanni al-thubut).
The hadith is used to argue that actions performed in error or forgetfulness are not sinful, and by extension, the worldly ruling of validity does not require intention.
3
Analyze the Hanafi interpretation of the text
Examine why the Hanafis depart from the literal meaning. They argue that a literal reading would imply that errors never occur—which is false. Therefore, a metaphorical meaning (majaz) is intended: removal of sin in the Hereafter, not removal of worldly consequences.
This step applies the usul principle that haqiqah is set aside when it leads to an impossible or absurd meaning, and majaz is adopted based on contextual indication (qarina).
4
Contrast with the Shafi'i reading
The Shafi'is interpret the hadith differently. They hold to the general (umum) meaning of the words, requiring intention in wudu based on other evidence. The text notes that the Shafi'is object to a metaphorical general meaning (umum majaz) as impermissible in their usul.
This highlights a foundational usul difference: the Hanafis accept majaz in general texts when context demands it; the Shafi'is restrict such metaphorical shift.
5
Derive the thamarah al-khilaf
Determine the practical consequence (thamarah al-khilaf) of the dispute. For Hanafis, wudu performed without intention is valid; for Shafi'is, it is invalid. This difference directly affects daily worship.
The dispute does not affect other acts of worship like salah and fasting, where intention is required by both schools.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ہمارے نزدیک تو اس لئے کہ اس صورت میں عموم مشترک لازم آئیگا اور امام شافعی کے نزدیک اس لئے کہ عموم مجاز لازم آئے گا اور یہ ان کے نزدیک جائز نہیں ہے ۔ حاصل کلام یہی ہے جواز اعمال نیت پر موقوف نہیں اسلئے احناف کے نزدیک وضو میں نیت فرض نہیں ہے امام شافعی کے نزدیک وضو میں نیت فرض ہے لیکن جو باقی عبادات مقصودہ ہیں وہ نیت کے بغیر صحیح نہیں ہوں گی۔ حضور صلی اللہ علیہ وسلم کا فرمان رفع عن امتى الخطاً والنسيان اس میں بھی حقیقت کو چھوڑا گیا ہے محل کلام کی دلالت کی وجہ سے کیونکہ اس کے ظاہر سے تو یہ معلوم ہوتا ہے کہ اس است سے خطا اور نسیان ہو ہی نہیں سکتا۔ حالانکہ یہ بات غلط ہے اس لئے یہاں مجازی معنی مراد ہو گا یعنی خطاء اور نسیان کی بناء پر آخرت میں گناہ نہیں ہو گا اگر چہ دنیا کا حکم اس پر بہر صورت مرتب ہو گا لہذا اگر خطاء روزے کی حالت میں کچھ کھا پی لیا تو روزہ فاسد ہو جائے گا اور خطاء نماز کی حالت میں کلام کیا تو نماز فاسد ہو جائے گی۔
According to us (Hanafis), because in this case a common general meaning would be necessary, and according to Imam Shafi'i, because a metaphorical general meaning would be necessary, and that is not permissible according to him. The summary of the discourse is that the permissibility of actions is not dependent on intention, therefore according to the Hanafis intention is not obligatory in wudu, while according to Imam Shafi'i intention is obligatory in wudu. As for the other intended acts of worship, they are not valid without intention. The saying of the Prophet (صلى الله عليه وسلم) 'رفع عن أمتي الخطأ والنسيان' — in this too the literal meaning has been left due to the indication of the context, because from its apparent meaning it would imply that error and forgetfulness cannot occur from this ummah, while this is wrong. Therefore a metaphorical meaning is intended here, i.e., on account of error and forgetfulness there will be no sin in the Hereafter, even though the worldly ruling will still apply. So if during fasting one mistakenly eats or drinks, the fast becomes invalid, and if during prayer one speaks mistakenly, the prayer becomes invalid.
Source pages p. 179

Commentary
This is a dispute between the Hanafi and Shafi'i schools regarding the obligation of intention (niyyah) in wudu. The Hanafi position is that intention is not fard in wudu because the permissibility of actions does not depend on it, as evidenced by the hadith 'رفع عن أمتي الخطأ والنسيان'. The Hanafis interpret this hadith metaphorically: it means that there is no sin for error or forgetfulness, but the worldly rulings (like invalidity of fast or prayer) still apply. Therefore, wudu performed without intention is valid. The Shafi'is, on the other hand, argue that intention is required in wudu based on a different understanding of 'umum' (generality). The text refutes the Shafi'i view by explaining that the hadith's apparent meaning would be absurd (that errors never occur), so a metaphorical interpretation is necessary, which does not negate the worldly ruling.

Key Terms
حقیقت (haqiqah): Literal meaning; using a word in its original sense.
مجاز (majaz): Metaphorical meaning; using a word in other than its original sense due to context.
عموم (umum): General term that applies to all individuals of a category.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi position presented in the text, why is intention not fard in wudu?
A) Because the hadith 'رفع عن أمتي الخطأ والنسيان' shows that errors are not sinful, so wudu without intention is valid.
B) Because wudu is a mere cleaning act and does not require intention.
C) Because the Shafi'i school agrees that intention is not required.
D) Because the Qur'an does not mention intention for wudu.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school holds that intention is not fard in wudu based on a metaphorical interpretation of the hadith 'رفع عن أمتي الخطأ والنسيان', distinguishing between worldly validity and sin in the Hereafter.

The Literal Prohibition of Substances: A Hanafi Usul Dispute
Hanafi position that prohibition attributed to substances is literal (haqiqah) against those who say it is metaphorical (majaz).

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why the Hanafi school holds that prohibition attributed to substances is literal (haqiqah) and evaluate the opposing argument that it is metaphorical (majaz).

Core Idea
Prohibition can be literal for substances because it has two types: one targeting the action, one targeting the entity itself.

When Allah says 'حرمت عليكم أمهاتكم' or the Prophet said 'حرمت الخمر لعينها', are these prohibitions literal or metaphorical? Some scholars argue that prohibition only applies to actions, not substances, so such phrases must be interpreted metaphorically. The Hanafi school, however, maintains that the prohibition is literal, relying on a distinction between two types of prohibition. This lesson unpacks that argument and its practical consequences.

Guided Path
1
State the dispute
Identify the two positions: the Hanafi view that tahrim attributed to substances is haqiqah, and the opposing view that it is majaz.
2
Examine the opposing argument
Understand the opponents' reasoning: prohibition is an attribute of actions, not substances; therefore, phrases like 'حرمت الخمر لعينها' must be interpreted metaphorically as 'prohibition of drinking wine'.
3
Analyze the Hanafi rebuttal
Learn the Hanafi distinction: two types of tahrim—one directed at the action (making the act prohibited) and one directed at the entity (which implies prohibition of all related actions and is more emphatic).
This second type is likened to negation of the entity, which is stronger than mere negation of the action.
4
Identify the thamarah al-khilaf
Determine the practical difference: does the prohibition of wine affect rulings on impurity and sale, or just the act of drinking?
The Hanafi position leads to broader implications for the substance itself.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : والتحريم المضاف إلى الأعيان كالممحارم والخمر حقيقة عندنا خلافاً للبعض
بعض لوگوں کا خیال ہے جب تحریم کی نسبت اعیان کی طرف کی جائے جیسا کہ اللہ تعالیٰ کے اس قول میں حرمت علیکم امھا تکم.... الخ اور اس حدیث میں حرمت الخمر لعینھا تو یہ باں مجاز مراد ہو گا یعنی حرمت علیکم نکاح امھا تکم اور حرمت شرب الخمر لعینھا کیونکہ خمر تو عین ہے وہ حرمت کو قبول نہیں کرتا کیونکہ حالت اور حرمت فعل کے اوصاف ہیں
ہم کہتے ہیں کہ حرمت اپنی حقیقت پر ہے اس لئے کہ حرمت کی دو قسمیں ہیں: (1) دو حرمت جو فعل کی طرف متوجہ ہو تو فعل ممنوع عنہ بن جائے گا اور بندہ ممنوع ۔ (۲) وہ حرمت جو گل کی طرف متوجہ ہوتی ہے تو فعل ممنوع بن جاتا ہے اور بندہ ممنوع عنہ اور منع کرنے میں اس میں دونوں وجہوں سے زیادہ مبالغہ پایا جاتا ہے اس لئے کہ یہ تو بمنز رفی کے بن گئی اور نفی میں نہیں سے زیادہ مبالغہ پایا جاتا ہے۔
His saying: 'And prohibition attributed to substances like mothers and wine is literal according to us, contrary to some.' Some people think that when prohibition is attributed to substances, as in Allah's saying 'حرمت عليكم أمهاتكم' and in the hadith 'حرمت الخمر لعينها', then it is metaphorical, meaning 'حرمت عليكم نكاح أمهاتكم' and 'حرمت شرب الخمر لعينها', because wine is a substance and it does not accept prohibition, as states and prohibitions are attributes of actions. We say that prohibition is upon its literal meaning because prohibition has two types: (1) prohibition that is directed towards the action, so the action becomes the prohibited thing and the servant is prohibited; (2) the prohibition that is directed towards the entity, so the action becomes prohibited and the servant is prohibited from the action, and in this there is greater emphasis because it is like the negation of the entity, and there is more emphasis in negation than in 'not'.
Source pages p. 179

Commentary
This passage addresses a dispute about whether prohibition (tahrim) when attributed directly to substances (like wine or mothers) is literal or metaphorical. The Hanafi school holds that it is literal (haqiqah). The opponents (some scholars) argue that prohibition is an attribute of actions, not substances, so attributing it to substances requires metaphorical interpretation (e.g., 'حرمت الخمر لعينها' means 'drinking wine is prohibited'). The Hanafis rebut this by distinguishing two types of prohibition: one directed at the action (making the action prohibited) and another directed at the entity (making the entity itself prohibited, which implies prohibition of related actions). The second type is more emphatic and is literal, as it is akin to negating the entity itself. Therefore, phrases like 'حرمت عليكم أمهاتكم' are literal prohibitions of the act of marrying them, but the attribution to the mother is direct and real.

Key Terms
تحریم (tahrim): Prohibition; a legal ruling that an act or substance is forbidden.
حقیقت (haqiqah): Literal usage; a word used in its original meaning.
مجاز (majaz): Metaphorical usage; a word used in other than its original meaning.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi position in the text, how many types of prohibition (tahrim) are there?
A) One: prohibition directed at actions.
B) Two: one directed at actions, one directed at entities.
C) Three: actions, entities, and states.
D) None: prohibition is always metaphorical.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school holds that prohibition attributed to substances is literal because it is a second type of tahrim directed at the entity itself, making the prohibition more emphatic.

Ikhtilaf — Scholarly Disagreement

The Meaning of Waw in Conjunction: Hanafi vs Shafi'i
Hanafi position that waw is for absolute conjunction without sequence or simultaneity.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why the Hanafi school holds that waw indicates absolute conjunction and evaluate the Shafi'i argument for sequence.

Core Idea
The particle waw (و) does not imply sequence; sequence must be proven from external evidence, not the conjunction itself.

In this lesson, we examine a foundational usul al-fiqh dispute between the Hanafis and Shafi'is regarding the meaning of the Arabic particle waw (و) when used for conjunction. The Hanafis argue that waw simply indicates partnership in the ruling without any order or simultaneity, while Imam Shafi'i and others claim it implies sequence. We will analyze the proofs from the Quran and Sunnah, and see how the Hanafis respond with counter-examples.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
The Hanafis hold that waw is for absolute conjunction (مطلق العطف) without any implication of sequence or simultaneity; it merely indicates partnership in the ruling (شركة).
This applies whether conjoining single words or sentences.
2
Identify the Shafi'i objection and its proof
Imam Shafi'i argues that waw indicates sequence (tartib), citing Quranic verses like 'إن الصفا والمروة' and 'واركعوا واسجدوا' where an order of actions is observed.
These texts appear to demand a specific order.
3
Analyze the Hanafi response to the Shafi'i proof
The Hanafis respond that the sequence in those texts is known from external sources (e.g., the order of revelation or the Prophet's practice), not from the waw itself. They also point to the Quranic verse 'واسجدي واركعي' where prostration is mentioned before bowing, showing that waw does not enforce order.
This demonstrates that waw is neutral regarding sequence.
4
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf (practical consequence)
In fiqh, for example, in divorce pronouncements like 'أنت طالق وطالق وطالق', Hanafis rule only one divorce occurs because waw does not imply repetition; Shafi'is may count multiple divorces if sequence is assumed.
The difference affects contracts, oaths, and any statement using waw.
5
Evaluate the tarjih (preferring the Hanafi position)
The Hanafi position is textually supported by the presence of both orders in the Quran; the Shafi'i claim of sequence cannot be sustained by the particle alone. Therefore, the Hanafi view is relied upon.
The burden of proof lies on those claiming sequence from the waw.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : ويتصل بماذكر ناحروف المعاني فالواؤ لمطلق العطف من غير تعرض لمقارنة ولا ترتيب .
حقیقت اور مجاز کے ساتھ حروف معانی بھی متصل ہوتے ہیں کیونکہ حروف معانی اگر اپنے معنی موضوع لہ میں استعمال ہوں تو حقیقت ہو نگے اور اگر غیر معنی موضوع لہ میں استعمال ہوں تو مجاز ہو نگے ان میں واو کو مقدم کیا۔
السواف : واد مطلق عطف کیلئے آتا ہے یعنی مطلق شرکت کیلئے تو اگر مفرد کا مفرد پر عطف ہو تو شرکت صرف محکوم علیہ یا صرف محکوم بہ میں ہوگی اور اگر جملہ کا عطف جملہ پر ہوتو شرکت ثبوت اور وجود میں ہوگی ۔
لیکن بعض لوگ کہتے ہیں کہ واؤ مقارنت اور اجتماع پر دلالت کرتی ہے
اور امام شافعی فرماتے ہیں کہ واؤ ترتیب پر دلالت کرتی ہے ان کی دلیل ان الصفا والمروۃ اور حضور کا ارشادن بنداً بما بعد اللہ اور دوسری جگہ ہے وار کفو واسجدوا اور ظاہر ہے کہ صفار کو مردہ پر اور رکوع کو مجود پر مقدم کرنا ضروری ہے۔ پہلی دلیل کا جواب یہ ہو سکتا ہے کہ ہم نے ترتیب وحی متلو سے جان لی ہے اور اس آیت کا حوالہ اس لئے دیا کیا ہے کہ تقدیم فی الذکر اہتمام سے خالی نہیں ہے۔ اور دوسری دلیل کا جواب یہ ہے کہ قرآن میں دوسری جگہ آتا ہے واسجدی وار کھی حالانکہ بجد داتور کوٹ سے مقدم نہیں ہوتا۔
His saying: 'And connected to what has been mentioned is the discussion of particles of meaning, for the waw is for absolute conjunction without indicating simultaneity or sequence.' The particles of meaning are also connected with reality and metaphor, because if particles of meaning are used in their original meaning, they are real, and if used in other than their original meaning, they are metaphorical. Among them, waw is given priority. The waw is for absolute conjunction, i.e., for absolute partnership. So if a single word is conjoined to a single word, partnership is only in the subject or only in the predicate; if a sentence is conjoined to a sentence, partnership is in affirmation and existence. But some people say that waw indicates simultaneity and combination, and Imam Shafi'i says that waw indicates sequence. Their proof is the verse 'إن الصفا والمروة' and the Prophet's saying 'بنداً بما بعد الله' and in another place 'واركعوا واسجدوا', and it is obvious that starting with Safa before Marwah and bowing before prostrating is necessary. The answer to the first proof is that we know the sequence from the order of revelation, and this verse is cited because precedence in mention is not free from emphasis. And the answer to the second proof is that in the Quran in another place it says 'واسجدي واركعي' while bowing does not come before prostration.
Source pages p. 180

Commentary
This passage discusses the meaning of the particle waw (و) when used for conjunction ('atf). The Hanafi position is that waw indicates absolute conjunction (جمع مطلق) without implying any order (tartib) or simultaneity (muqaranat). It simply means partnership in the ruling. The text explains that if waw conjoins two words, they share the same subject or predicate; if it conjoins two sentences, they share in existence or affirmation. Some people and Imam Shafi'i argue that waw indicates sequence (tartib). They cite examples like 'إن الصفا والمروة' (ordering of Safa and Marwah) and 'واركعوا واسجدوا' (order of bowing and prostrating in prayer). The Hanafi response is that the sequence in these texts is known from other sources (like the order of revelation or the actual practice), not from the waw itself. They further point out that the Quran has 'واسجدي واركعي' (with prostration before bowing), showing that waw does not require order.

Key Terms
واو (waw): The Arabic letter and particle used for conjunction.
عطف ('atf): Grammatical conjunction; joining two elements in a sentence.
ترتیب (tartib): Sequence or order.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the Hanafi position on the meaning of waw in conjunction?
A) Waw indicates sequence (tartib).
B) Waw indicates simultaneity (muqaranat).
C) Waw indicates absolute conjunction without sequence or simultaneity.
D) Waw indicates exclusivity.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school holds that waw indicates absolute conjunction; any sequence must be proven from external evidence, not the particle itself.

The Particle Thumma: Break vs Delay in Hanafi Usul
Usul dispute on thumma in Hanafi divorce law

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi dispute between Imam Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn regarding the particle thumma in conditional divorce and apply the correct ruling according to each view.

Core Idea
Thumma creates a break: Imam sees independence; Sahibayn see only delay in ruling.

This passage examines the usul principle governing the particle thumma (then) in marriage dissolutions. While thumma normally indicates a delay, the Hanafi school is split on whether that delay severs the unity of the sentence or merely postpones the legal effect. The practical difference emerges in a conditional divorce formula.

Guided Path
1
Identify the linguistic function of thumma
Recognize that thumma signals a temporal delay (tarakhi) between two events. The key question is whether this delay separates the statements into independent units or merely delays the legal effect within a continuous statement.
Contrast with fa which implies immediate succession.
2
Understand the two interpretations
Imam Abu Hanifa: thumma implies a complete break (sukut) so each subsequent statement is independent. The Sahibayn: thumma only delays the ruling; the entire sentence remains a single pronouncement.
The linguistic argument hinges on whether thumma restarts speech or just postpones the hukm.
3
Apply to the conditional divorce example
Consider the statement: 'You are divorced, then divorced, then divorced, if you enter the house' to a non-consummated wife. Determine the outcome under each view.
Non-consummated wife: first divorce is irrevocable; subsequent divorces have no effect once irrevocable divorce has occurred.
4
Trace the thamarah al-khilaf
Under Imam Abu Hanifa, the first divorce is immediate and unconditional; the rest are void because they are conditional but cannot apply after irrevocable divorce. Under the Sahibayn, all three divorces are conditional on entry; if entry occurs, three divorces take effect (though with a non-consummated wife, only one counts? The text suggests the Sahibayn would still treat them as conditional).
The practical consequence affects the number of divorces actually occurring.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : وثم للتراخى بمنزلة ما لو سكت ثم استأنف حتى اذا قال لغير المدخول بها أنت طالق ثم طالق ثم طالق ان دخلت الدار فعنده الاول ويلغو ما بعده ولو قدم الشرط تعلق الاول به ووقع الثاني ولغا الثالث . یم : ثم تراخی کیلئے آتا ہے گو یا متکلم خاموش ہو گیا اور اس نے پھر نئے سرے سے کلام کیا مثلا اگر کسی نے اپنی بیوی سے کہا انت طالق ثم طالق تو یوں سمجھا جائیگا کہ یہ انت حالق کہہ کر خاموش ہو گیا اور اسکے بعد اس نے ثم طالق کہا امام صاحب کے نزدیک یہاں ابھی تعلیم اور حکم دنوں میں ہے جبکہ صاحبین کہتے ہیں کہ صرف تراخی فی الحکم ہے اس اختلاف کا نتیجہ یہ نکلے گا کہ اگر کسی شخص نے اپنی غیر مدخولہ بیوی سے کہا انت طالق ثم طالق ثم طالق ان دخلت الدار تو امام صاحب کے نزدیک پہلی طلاق واقع ہو جائیگی اور باقی طلاقیں انفو جا ئیں گی کیونکہ جب وہ
He said: And thumma is for delay, like if one is silent then resumes. So when he says to a non-consummated wife: 'You are divorced, then divorced, then divorced, if you enter the house,' according to him (Imam Abu Hanifa), the first (divorce) occurs and what follows is void. And if he presents the condition, the first (divorce) is attached to it, the second occurs, and the third is void. Thumma: Thumma comes for delay, as if the speaker became silent and then started anew. For example, if someone said to his wife: 'You are divorced, then divorced,' it is understood that he said 'You are divorced' and became silent, then after that he said 'then divorced.' According to Imam (Abu Hanifa), here there is both teaching (ta'lim) and ruling (hukm), while the Two Companions (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) say that it is only delay in the ruling (tarakhi fi al-hukm). The consequence of this difference is that if a man said to his non-consummated wife: 'You are divorced, then divorced, then divorced, if you enter the house,' according to Imam, the first divorce occurs and the remaining divorces become void, because when he...
Source pages p. 186

Commentary
This passage discusses the particle thumma (ثم) which indicates delay (tarakhi). It is like a pause and resumption of speech. The key issue is whether thumma separates independent statements or merely delays the legal effect within a single statement. Imam Abu Hanifa holds that thumma implies a complete break, so each statement after thumma is a new independent declaration. The Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani) hold that thumma only delays the legal consequence, but the statement is considered continuous. The practical difference appears in conditional divorce with a non-consummated wife (ghayr madkhul biha). For example, if a man says: 'You are divorced, then divorced, then divorced, if you enter the house' (a conditional statement at the end). According to Imam Abu Hanifa, the first divorce ('You are divorced') is effective immediately because it is not conditional (the condition comes after thumma, thus separate). The second and third are void because they are part of the condition? Actually the text says: 'according to him, the first occurs and what follows is void' because the condition likely attaches to the last? The text is cut off, but the general rule is that with thumma, the first divorce is immediate, and the subsequent ones are postponed and subject to the condition. However, since a non-consummated wife cannot be revocably divorced after the first, the subsequent divorces are impossible? This is a subtle Hanafi dispute. The authority weight is from the Hanafi school's ikhtilaf between Imam and the Sahibayn, a standard topic in usul al-fiqh.

Key Terms
ثم (thumma): A conjunction particle indicating delay (tarakhi), often implying a pause or sequence with a time gap.
تراخي (tarakhi): Delay or postponement in time between two events or statements.

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) All three divorces are conditional on entry.
B) The first divorce is immediate and the rest are void.
C) The first two divorces are immediate and the third is conditional.
D) No divorce occurs until entry.

Key Takeaway
The particle thumma can indicate either a break or mere delay; the Hanafi school is divided, and the practical difference appears in conditional divorce.

Ikhtilaf — Scholarly Disagreement
intermediate
8 min
Hanafi vs Sahibayn on Multiple Conditional Divorces with Fa and Thumma
Ruling on multiple conditional divorces with dispute

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on multiple conditional divorces using 'fa' and 'thumma' and explain the disagreement of the Sahibayn, including the thamarah al-khilaf.

Core Idea
In Hanafi usul, 'fa' and 'thumma' alter divorce timing; Sahibayn attach all three to the condition.

This passage deals with a nuanced issue in conditional divorces: how do the letters 'fa' (then/immediately) and 'thumma' (then with delay) affect multiple divorces when a condition is present? The Hanafi school, through Imam Abu Hanifa, distinguishes between the order of presentation, while the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) hold a different view. Understanding this ikhtilaf sharpens your ability to analyze how linguistic particles ('fa', 'thumma') interact with legal conditions in Hanafi usul al-fiqh.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and the general Hanafi rule
The husband pronounces three divorces with 'fa' or 'thumma' after a condition (e.g., 'If you enter the house, you are divorced, then divorced, then divorced'). The general Hanafi rule: the first divorce attaches to the condition; the second occurs immediately upon condition fulfillment; the third does not occur because the 'place' for divorce (the wife's marital bond) is already exhausted by the first two divorces.
This applies when the consequence (the divorces) is presented first. When the condition is presented first, the rule changes.
2
Understand the 'benefit' scenario
If the first divorce is suspended (condition unfulfilled), the marriage ends after the second divorce. If the husband remarries her and then the condition is fulfilled, the previously suspended divorces (the first two) fall immediately upon fulfillment, even though there was a new marriage. This shows the earlier attachment persists.
This demonstrates the legal effect of attaching divorces to a condition.
3
State the Sahibayn's position
The Sahibayn hold that all three divorces are attached to the condition and occur in order upon fulfillment. For a consummated wife, all three occur; for a non-consummated wife, only the first occurs (making her irrevocably divorced), and the others are ineffective because she was already separated.
The Sahibayn do not distinguish based on order of presentation; all three are suspended.
4
Analyze Imam Abu Hanifa's distinction based on order of presentation
Imam Abu Hanifa differentiates: (a) If the consequence (divorces) is presented first (e.g., 'You are divorced, then divorced, then divorced, if you enter the house'), then the first two divorces occur immediately, and the third is suspended on the condition. (b) If the condition is presented first (e.g., 'If you enter the house, you are divorced, then divorced, then divorced'), then the first divorce is suspended, and the second and third occur immediately.
This distinction relies on the linguistic function of 'fa' (immediate sequence) and 'thumma' (delayed sequence) and the principle that after two divorces, the third lacks a subject to fall upon.
5
Identify the thamarah al-khilaf (practical consequence)
In the case where the consequence is presented first (and the wife is consummated): Hanafi says first two occur immediately, third suspended; Sahibayn say all three are suspended. This affects whether the wife becomes irrevocably divorced immediately or only after condition fulfillment.
The dispute is about whether the second divorce operates immediately or is also suspended.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
انت طالق کہہ کر خاموش ہو گیا تو بعد والی طلاق کیلئے محل باقی نہیں رہا لہذا وہ اور ہو گئی اور اگر اسے فا یا ثم کو متقدم کیا اور یوں کہا ان دخلت الدار فأنت طالق ثم طالق ثم طالق تو پھر طلاق شروط سے ملحق ہو جائیگی اور دوسری واقع ہو جائیگی اور تیسری نہ ہو جائے گی اور پہلی کے محق یا معلق ہونے کا فائدہ یہ ہے کہ اگر نکاح ثانی کے بعد دوبارہ اس عورت کے بضع کا مالک بنا اور شرط پا کی گی تو تعلق سابق کی وجہ سے سابق دو طلاق واقع ہو جائینگی۔
صاحبین کا اختلاف نقل کیا گیا ہے۔ صاحبین فرماتے ہیں کہ تینوں طلاقیں شرط سے متعلق ہوں گی اور پھر وجود شرط کے بعد ترتیب سے واقع ہونگی۔ پھر اگر وہ عورت مدخولہ ہے تو تینوں طلاقیں واقع ہو جائیگی اور اگر وہ غیر مدخولہ ہے تو وہ پہلی سے بائنہ ہو جائے گی اور دوسری اور تیسری طلاق واقع نہیں ہوگی لیکن امام صاحب کے نزدیک اگر وہ مدخولہ ہے تو اگر جزاء مقدم ہو تو پہلی اور دوسری طلاق فی الحال واقع ہو جائے گی اور تیسری طلاق شرط سے معلق ہوگی اور اگر شرط مقدم ہو تو پہلی طلاق شرط سے متعلق ہوگی اور دوسری اور تیسری طلاق فی الحال واقع ہو جائیگی۔
If he said 'you are divorced' and remained silent, then there is no room left for the subsequent divorce, so it occurs. And if he preceded the 'fa' or 'thumma' and said: 'If you enter the house, you are divorced, then divorced, then divorced' then the divorces will be attached to the condition, the second will occur, and the third will not occur. The benefit of the first being effective or suspended is that if after a second marriage he again becomes owner of her vagina and the condition is fulfilled, then due to the previous attachment, the previous two divorces will occur. The disagreement of the Sahibayn is narrated. The Sahibayn say: All three divorces will be attached to the condition and then after occurrence of the condition they will occur in order. Then if she is a woman who has been consummated, all three divorces will occur; if she is not consummated, she becomes irrevocably divorced with the first, and the second and third do not occur. However, according to Imam Abu Hanifa, if she is consummated: if the consequence is presented first, then the first and second divorces occur immediately, and the third is suspended on the condition; if the condition is presented first, the first divorce is attached to the condition, and the second and third occur immediately.
Source pages p. 187

Commentary
This passage is a ruling on multiple conditional divorces using the words 'fa' and 'thumma'. It first states the general ruling: if a man says 'you are divorced' and stops, no further divorce can occur. But if he uses a conditional phrase like 'if you enter the house, you are divorced, then divorced, then divorced', then the divorces are attached to the condition. The second divorce occurs immediately upon the condition, but the third does not because the first two have already taken effect. The benefit of the first divorce being either immediate or suspended is explained: if after the conditional divorce the wife is divorced (first divorce not effective yet because of condition), then the man remarries her and the condition is fulfilled later, the two divorces that were suspended will now fall. This is the Hanafi position. Then the passage reports the disagreement of Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani (the Sahibayn). They hold that all three divorces are attached to the condition and occur in sequence upon fulfillment. If the wife is consummated, all three occur; if not, only the first occurs and she becomes irrevocably divorced. Imam Abu Hanifa distinguishes between presenting the consequence first (then first two occur immediately, third is suspended) and presenting the condition first (then first is suspended, second and third occur immediately).

Key Terms
فا (fa): A letter of sequence indicating immediate succession without delay.
ثم (thumma): A letter indicating sequence with a delay.
مدخولہ (madkhulah): A woman with whom marriage has been consummated.
جاء (jaza'): Consequence, result clause in a conditional sentence (e.g., 'you are divorced').
شرط (shart): Condition, the 'if' clause.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the practical difference (thamarah al-khilaf) between Imam Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn when a man says to his consummated wife 'You are divorced, then divorced, then divorced, if you enter the house'?
A) Abu Hanifa says all three are suspended; Sahibayn say first two occur immediately.
B) Abu Hanifa says first two occur immediately and third suspended; Sahibayn say all three are suspended.
C) Both agree that all three are suspended.
D) Abu Hanifa says all three occur immediately; Sahibayn say all three are suspended.

Key Takeaway
In multiple conditional divorces with 'fa' and 'thumma', Imam Abu Hanifa distinguishes between presenting the consequence first (first two immediate, third suspended) and presenting the condition first (first suspended, second and third immediate), unlike the Sahibayn who attach all three to the condition.

Interpreting 'Thumma' in the Expiation Hadith: Hanafi vs. Shafi'i
Analyses the hadith on expiation, arguing 'thumma' means 'waw'

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why the Hanafi school interprets 'thumma' (then) as 'waw' (and) in the hadith on expiation, and evaluate the Shafi'i counter-argument using principles of usul al-fiqh.

Core Idea
A particle's metaphorical meaning can preserve the real obligation of a command.

In this lesson, we examine a classic usul dispute between the Hanafi and Shafi'i schools over the meaning of 'thumma' (then) in the prophetic hadith about expiation for an oath. The Hanafi school argues that 'thumma' here is used metaphorically to mean 'waw' (and), based on the principle of preserving the real sense of a command and avoiding contradiction with other evidence. This dispute illustrates the interplay between literal and metaphorical interpretation of particles in the derivation of rulings.

Guided Path
1
Identify the disputed text
Locate the hadith under discussion: 'Let him expiate his oath, then let him come to that which is better.' Note that the word 'thumma' (then) is the point of contention.
The hadith is a dalil naqli, but its wording ('thumma') triggers the usul analysis.
2
State the Shafi'i position and its basis
Imam al-Shafi'i takes 'thumma' literally, implying sequence: expiation before the better act. This leads to the ruling that expiation before breaking the oath is permissible.
The Shafi'i rely on the literal meaning of particles unless there is a strong reason to depart.
3
State the Hanafi position and its dalil
Hanafis argue that 'thumma' is metaphorical ('waw') here to avoid making the command 'let him expiate' obligate expiation before the act, which no one holds. They cite another hadith or general principle of avoiding contradiction.
The Hanafi proof: if 'thumma' is literal, the command would be obligatory – but it's not, so the particle must be reinterpreted.
4
Analyze the Hanafi preference for metaphorical particle vs. metaphorical command
The Hanafi response prioritizes taking a metaphorical meaning in the particle ('thumma' as 'waw') rather than taking a metaphorical meaning in the command (which would lessen its obligation). This is a key usul principle.
This decision is based on the Hanafi hierarchy: real command > real particle; if one must be metaphorical, the particle is sacrificed.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf (practical difference)
Shafi'i: expiation may precede the better act (i.e., before breaking the oath). Hanafi: expiation is not required to precede the act; the command to expiate is not temporal sequential but merely conjunctional.
The practical effect shows the importance of the particle's interpretation.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : وفى قوله عليه السلام فليكفر عن يمنيه ثم ليأت با لذي هو خير استعير بمعنى الواو عملا بحقيقة الأمر تدل عليه الرواية.
سوال سوال ہوتا ہے کہ امام شافعی فرماتے ہیں کفارہ بالمال کو حنث پر مقدم کرنا جائز ہے اسلئے کہ حضور صلی اللہ علیہ وسلم نے فرمایا من حلف على يمين فرأى غيرها خيراً منها فليكفر عن يمينه ثم ليات بالذى هو خير او كما قال عليه الصلوة والسلام) - اتیان خیر حانث ہونے سے کنایہ ہے اور اسکو آپ نے ثم کے لفظ کے ساتھ کفارہ کے بعد ذکر کیا ہے تو معلوم ہوا کہ کفار بالمال کو حنث پر مقدم کرنا جائز ہے۔
جواب اگر ہم یہاں پر ثم کو اس کی حقیقت پر رکھیں تو حقیقت امر بر عمل کہ ناممکن نہیں رہے گا کیونکہ فليكفر امر ہے امر حقیقتہ وجوب کیلئے آتا ہے حالانکہ کسی کے نزدیک بھی کفارے کو مقدم کرنا واجب نہیں ہے۔ اگر کوئی کہے ثم کو حقیقی معنی پر برقرار رکھ کر امر کو مجازی معنی میں کیوں لیتے ہو تو اس کے دو جواب دیئے جاتے ہیں :
پہلا جواب .... دوسری حدیث اس پر دلالت کرتی ہے غم و او کے معنی میں ہے نا کہ حدیث کا چھوڑ ٹالا زم نہ آئے اسلئے شوافع والی حدیث میں مجازی طور پر ثم کو واو کے معنی میں لیں گے اور دوسری حدیث جس میں حانث ہونا مقدم ہے اسکو ثم کے اصل پر رکھیں گے تا کہ امر کی حقیقت و جوب فوت نہ ہو ۔
دوسرا جواب ...... حروف میں مجاز مراد لینا زیادہ بہتر ہے بجائے اس کے کہ امر میں مجازی معنی مراد لیا جائے لہذا ثم کو مجازی معنی پر محمول کیا جائے گا ۔
His saying: And in his (peace be upon him) saying: 'Let him expiate his oath, then let him come to that which is better' it is used metaphorically in the meaning of 'waw' as an operation on the reality of the command, as the narration indicates. A question is raised: Imam al-Shafi'i says that expiation with property before breaking the oath is permissible because the Prophet (peace be upon him) said: 'Whoever swears an oath and then sees something better than it, let him expiate his oath, then let him do that which is better' – 'doing the better' is a metaphor for breaking the oath, and he mentioned it with the word 'thumma' after expiation, so it is known that expiation with property before breaking the oath is permissible. Answer: If we take 'thumma' here in its real meaning, the reality of the command to act will not become impossible, because 'let him expiate' is a command, and a command is essentially for obligation, yet no one says expiation before breaking is obligatory. If someone says: why do you keep 'thumma' on its real meaning and take the command metaphorically? Two answers are given: First answer: Another hadith indicates that 'thumma' is in the meaning of 'waw', so that the hadith does not become contradictory. Therefore, in the Shafi'i hadith, we take 'thumma' metaphorically as 'waw', and in the other hadith where breaking the oath is given precedence, we keep 'thumma' on its original meaning so that the reality of obligation in the command is not lost. Second answer: Taking a metaphorical meaning in particles is better than taking a metaphorical meaning in the command; therefore, 'thumma' will be taken in its metaphorical meaning.
Source pages p. 187

Commentary
This passage is a usul dispute between the Hanafi school and Imam al-Shafi'i concerning the interpretation of the word 'thumma' (then) in the hadith about expiation. The hadith states: 'Whoever swears an oath and then sees something better, let him expiate his oath, then let him come to that which is better.' Shafi'i argues that 'thumma' indicates order, so one may expiate before breaking the oath (or before doing the better act), thus expiation prior to the act is permissible. The Hanafi response uses a two-fold argument. First, they argue that if 'thumma' is taken literally, it would imply that expiation is obligatory (since 'falyukaffir' is a command), but no one holds such obligation. Therefore, to avoid contradiction with another hadith that gives precedence to the oath-breaking, 'thumma' here is taken metaphorically to mean 'waw' (and), which does not imply sequence. Second, it is more appropriate to take a particle metaphorically than to take a command metaphorically. Thus, the Hanafi school interprets 'thumma' as 'waw' in this context, preserving the non-obligatory status of expiation.

Key Terms
ثم (thumma): A particle indicating sequence with delay; in this context interpreted metaphorically as 'waw'.
واو (waw): A particle of conjunction without implying sequence.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why do Hanafi scholars interpret 'thumma' as 'waw' in the hadith about expiation?
A) To make expiation obligatory
B) To avoid the implication that expiation is obligatory
C) Because Imam Shafi'i said so
D) Because 'thumma' never means sequence

Key Takeaway
When the literal meaning of a particle leads to an unacceptable obligation, it may be reinterpreted metaphorically, preserving the real meaning of the command.

Two Answers Regarding the Particle 'و' and the Command (Amr) in Hanafi Usul
Hanafi response to Shafi'i interpretation of waaw and amr in hadith

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi principle of preferring the real meaning of particles over metaphorical interpretation of commands in hadith conflicts, and construct the two answers used in response to the Shafi'i position.

Core Idea
Preserve the particle's real meaning; interpret the command metaphorically when hadiths conflict.

When two hadiths appear to conflict, usul al-fiqh provides principles to reconcile them. A key dispute between Hanafis and Shafi'is concerns whether to preserve the literal meaning of the particle 'و' (and) or the imperative form (amr). This passage explains the Hanafi preference for keeping the particle's real meaning and interpreting the command figuratively, with two compelling answers.

Guided Path
1
Identify the core conflict
Recognize that both the particle 'و' (meaning 'and') and the command (amr) have real (haqiqi) meanings. When a hadith uses a phrase like 'talaq and divorce', a conflict may arise if another hadith indicates a different interpretation. Determine which element should retain its real meaning.
The conflict is between preserving the literal conjunction or the literal obligation.
2
State the opposing view
The Shafi'i school prefers to keep the amr in its real meaning (indicating obligation) and interprets the particle 'و' metaphorically (e.g., as 'or' or for inclusion). Understand this as the alternative.
3
Analyze the first Hanafi answer
Use a second hadith that indicates the intended meaning of the particle. By prioritizing that second hadith, the particle in the first hadith is taken metaphorically, while the amr remains in its real meaning in the second hadith. This avoids abandoning any hadith.
The first answer relies on reconciling multiple hadiths.
4
Analyze the second Hanafi answer
Metaphorical interpretation of particles is more acceptable than metaphorical interpretation of commands because the real meaning of the command is weightier for law. Therefore, apply metaphor to the particle when necessary, preserving the command's real meaning.
This answer establishes a general principle: metaphor in particles is preferable to metaphor in commands.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
واجب نہیں ہے۔ اگر کوئی کہے تم کو حقیقی معنی پر برقرار رکھ کر امر کو مجازی معنی میں کیوں لیتے ہو تو اس کے دو جواب دیئے جاتے ہیں : پہلا جواب .... دوسری حدیث اس پر دلالت کرتی ہے غم و او کے معنی میں ہے نا کہ حدیث کا چھوڑ ٹالا زم نہ آئے اسلئے شوافع والی حدیث میں مجازی طور پر تم کو واؤ کے معنی میں لیں گے اور دوسری حدیث جس میں حانث ہونا مقدم ہے اسکو تم کے اصل پر رکھیں گے تا کہ امر کی حقیقت و جنوب فوت نہ ہو ۔ دوسرا جواب ...... حروف میں مجاز مراد لینا زیادہ بہتر ہے بجائے اس کے کہ امر میں مجازی معنی مراد لیا جائے لہذا اتم کو مجازی معنی پر محمول کیا جائے گا ۔
It is not obligatory. If someone says: 'Why do you take the command (amr) in a metaphorical sense while keeping the [particle] on its real meaning?' then two answers are given: First answer ... the second hadith indicates that [the particle] is in the meaning of 'and' (waw) so that the hadith is not abandoned; therefore, in the Shafi'i hadith, we take [the particle] metaphorically in the meaning of 'and', and the second hadith in which breaking the oath is prioritized, we keep [the particle] on its original meaning so that the reality of the command is not lost. Second answer: taking metaphorical meaning in particles is better than taking metaphorical meaning in the command; therefore, 'anta' (you) will be carried on the metaphorical meaning.
Source pages p. 188

Commentary
This passage is a Hanafi response to a Shafi'i objection. The issue is about interpreting the particle 'و' (waaw) and the command (amr) when there is a potential conflict between two hadiths. The Hanafi position prefers to preserve the real meaning of 'و' (as conjunction) and interpret the command metaphorically if necessary. The two answers both uphold this priority. The first answer uses the principle that a second hadith indicates the intended meaning, and the second answer states that taking metaphorical meaning in particles is better than in commands.

Key Terms
و (waaw): The particle 'and', usually indicating conjunction
أمر (amr): Command, imperative form

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi usul, when two hadiths conflict, preserving the real meaning of the particle 'و' takes precedence over preserving the literal command; the command may be interpreted metaphorically.

The Hanafi Dispute on Metaphor: 'This is Free or This'
Explains disagreement between Imam Abu Hanifa and Sahibayn on metaphorical usage

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why Imam Abu Hanifa permits metaphor when literal meaning is impossible and apply this principle to analogous cases.

Core Idea
When literal meaning fails, metaphor saves the utterance—probability of specification is better than discarding.

This passage from Noor al-Anwar presents a classic usul dispute between Imam Abu Hanifa and his two disciples, Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani. The question is whether a statement like 'This is free or this' to a slave and an animal can be valid if the literal meaning is impossible because 'or' implies an unspecified referent. Understanding this disagreement reveals a foundational Hanafi principle about the permissibility of metaphor when the literal meaning leads to impossibility.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Contested Case
Consider the statement 'هذا حر أو هذا' addressed to a slave and an animal. What is the literal meaning? Why is it impossible?
The literal meaning is that one of the two unspecified entities is free, but manumission requires a specific person.
2
State the Sahibayn's Position
Abu Yusuf and Muhammad rule the statement invalid because the referent is unspecified and cannot be the locus of manumission.
3
State Imam Abu Hanifa's Position
Imam rules the statement valid by way of metaphor; the probability of specification imposes a duty on the speaker to clarify.
He analogizes to the case of two slaves where specification is required.
4
Locate the Usul Principle
The underlying principle: When literal meaning is impossible, can metaphor be employed? Imam says yes, Sahibayn say no.
This is a dispute about the scope of مجاز in usul al-fiqh.
5
Apply the Principle to an Analogous Case
Consider the case of two slaves where the master says 'One of you is free'. How do Imam and Sahibayn rule?
Imam: valid, must specify. Sahibayn: invalid.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : وقا لا اذا قال لعبده ودابته هذا حر أو هذا انه با طل لأنه اسم لأحدهما غير عين وذالك غير محل للعتق وعنده هو كذلك لكن على احتمال التعين حتى لزمه التعيين كما في مسألة العبدين والعمل بالمحتمل أولى من الاهدار وهما ينكر ان الاستعارة عند استحالة الحكم فهما جريا .
صاحبین فرماتے ہیں کہ اگر کسی شخص نے اپنے نام اور چوپائے کو کہا هذا حر أو هذا تو یہ کلام باطل ہوگا اسلئے کہ خدا کا مشار الیہ ان میں سے کسی غیر معین کو بنایا گیا ہے اور غیر معین محق کا محل نہیں بن سکتا، جبکہ امام صاحب کہتے ہیں کہ اگر چہ حقیقتا تو ایسے ہی ہے لیکن مجازا یہ تعین کا احتمال رکھتا ہے بند متکلم پرتعیین لازم ہوگی اصل میں یہ اختلاف اس اختلاف پر مبنی ہے کہ اگر حقیقت محال ہو تو امام صاحب کے نزدیک مجاز مراد لے سکتے ہے اور صاحبین کے نزدیک اس صورت میں مجاز مراد نہیں لے سکتے ۔
His saying: And they said: When he says to his slave and his animal 'This is free or this', it is invalid because it is a name for one of them unspecified, and that is not a place for manumission. And according to him (Imam) it is likewise but on the probability of specification so that specification becomes necessary for him, as in the issue of two slaves, and acting on what is probable is better than discarding. And they (Sahibayn) deny metaphor when ruling is impossible, so they proceed accordingly.
Source pages p. 193

Commentary
This passage presents a dispute in Hanafi usul regarding the use of metaphor when the literal meaning is impossible. The matn states that if a person says to his slave and his animal 'this is free or this', the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) rule it invalid because the phrase refers to an unspecified individual, and an unspecified referent cannot be the locus of manumission. Imam Abu Hanifa, however, argues that although literal specification is impossible, the word 'or' metaphorically implies specification, imposing on the speaker the duty to clarify. This is analogous to the case of two slaves where the speaker must specify. The underlying usul principle is: when literal meaning is impossible, Imam allows metaphor; Sahibayn do not. This dispute appears in the context of the particle 'aw' (or) and its metaphorical uses.

Key Terms
استعارة (isti'ārah): Metaphorical usage of a word from its literal meaning to another due to a relationship.
تعين (ta'yīn): Specification of the referent among possibilities.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) The statement is valid and the speaker must specify.
B) The statement is invalid because the referent is unspecified.
C) The statement is valid but only metaphorically.
D) The statement is valid only for the animal.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school allows metaphor to salvage an utterance when literal meaning is impossible, imposing specification on the speaker.

The Legal Effect of 'Bi-Mashiyat Allah' in Hanafi Usul
Linguistic analysis of a conditional divorce phrase.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the Hanafi linguistic principle that interprets 'bi' as a condition in divorce statements and apply it to derive the ruling that divorce does not occur.

Core Idea
When a husband says 'by the will of Allah,' the divorce is conditional upon Allah's will, so it does not take effect.

This passage examines the phrase 'أنت طالق بمشية الله' (you are divorced by the will of Allah). The author explains that the particle 'ب' here indicates a condition (shart), making the divorce dependent on Allah's will. Since Allah's will is unknown, the divorce does not occur. This ruling is based on a linguistic analysis of the particle and reflects a Hanafi usul principle that words are interpreted according to their customary usage.

Guided Path
1
Identify the key phrase and its components
The phrase is 'أنت طالق بمشية الله'. Focus on the particle 'ب' and the word 'مشية' (will).
The particle 'ب' has multiple meanings in Arabic.
2
Analyze the linguistic usage of 'ب'
Determine if 'ب' here is used literally (as an instrument) or figuratively (as a condition). The author says it means 'shart' (condition).
In oaths and conditions, 'ب' often introduces a clause.
3
Interpret the implied meaning (taqdir)
The author states the taqdir is 'أنت طالق إن شاء الله' (you are divorced if Allah wills). This shows the conditional nature.
4
Derive the ruling
Since the condition (Allah's will) is unknown, the divorce does not occur. The statement has no legal effect until the condition is met, which is impossible to know.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : وفي قوله أنت طالق بمشية الله تعالى بمعنى الشرط . اور اگر کوئی یوں کہے انت طالق بمشية الله تعالی تو تقدیر عبارت یوں ہوگی انت طالق انشاء اللہ تعالی لہذا طلاق واقع نہیں ہوگی۔
His saying: And in his saying 'You are divorced by the will of Allah Almighty' it means a condition. And if someone says 'You are divorced by the will of Allah Almighty' then the interpretation of the phrase is 'You are divorced if Allah wills', therefore divorce does not occur.
Source pages p. 199

Commentary
This passage is a ruling on the phrase 'أنت طالق بمشية الله' (you are divorced by the will of Allah). The author explains that the particle 'ب' here indicates a condition, similar to 'إن شاء الله' (if Allah wills). Therefore, the divorce is suspended upon Allah's will and since that is unknown, divorce does not take effect. This is a Hanafi position based on linguistic analysis of the particle.

Key Terms
بمشية الله (bi-mashiyatillah): A phrase meaning 'by the will of Allah', interpreted as a condition (shart) that suspends the divorce.
شرط (shart): A condition that suspends the occurrence of an action upon its fulfillment.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) One revocable divorce occurs immediately.
B) Divorce occurs only if Allah wills it, hence it does not occur.
C) Three divorces occur because it is an oath.
D) The divorce is suspended until the wife wills it.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school interprets 'bi-mashiyat Allah' as a condition, not an oath, resulting in no divorce.
